       <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="0" page="0"/>
      </pdf2:Link>
     </ns3:footnotemark>
     <ns3:footnote id="ID.00010" ref="[ID.00008]">
      <ns3:footnotelabel id="ID.00011">
       <pdf2:NonStruct id="ID.00013">
        <bfo:content mcid="102" page="0">1</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:NonStruct>
      </ns3:footnotelabel>
      <ns3:text class="center" id="ID.00012">
       <bfo:content mcid="103" page="0">fischer@troubleshooting-tex.de</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:footnote>
    </ns3:text>
    <ns3:text class="center" id="ID.00014">
     <bfo:content mcid="3" page="0">2023-05-16</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
  </pdf2:Title>
  <pdf2:Div id="ID.00015">
   <pdf2:Div id="ID.00016"/>
   <pdf2:Div id="ID.00017">
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00018">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00019">
      <bfo:content mcid="4" page="0">This package is not meant for normal document production. It is mainly a tool to </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Em id="ID.00020">
       <bfo:content mcid="5" page="0">research</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Em>
      <bfo:content mcid="6" page="0">tagging.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00021">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00022">
      <bfo:content mcid="7" page="0">You need a very current </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Span ActualText="LaTeX" id="ID.00023">
       <bfo:content mcid="8" page="0">LATEX</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Span>
      <bfo:content mcid="9" page="0"> format. You need a very current L3 programming layer. You need the new </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Span ActualText="LaTeX" id="ID.00024">
       <bfo:content mcid="10" page="0">LATEX</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Span>
      <bfo:content mcid="11" page="0"> PDF management bundle.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00025">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00026">
      <bfo:content mcid="12" page="0">This package is incomplete, experimental and quite probably contains bugs. It is in parts quite slow as the code prefers readability over speed. At some time it will disappear when the code has been integrated into the </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Span ActualText="LaTeX" id="ID.00027">
       <bfo:content mcid="13" page="0">LATEX</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Span>
      <bfo:content mcid="14" page="0"> format.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00028">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00029">
      <bfo:content mcid="15" page="0">This package can change in an incompatible way.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00030">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00031">
      <bfo:content mcid="16" page="0">You need some knowledge about </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Span ActualText="TeX" id="ID.00032">
       <bfo:content mcid="17" page="0">TEX</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Span>
      <bfo:content mcid="18" page="0">, PDF and perhaps even lua to use it.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00033">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00034">
      <bfo:content mcid="19" page="0">Issues, comments, suggestions should be added as issues to the github tracker:</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00035">
     <ns3:text class="center" id="ID.00036">
      <pdf2:Link id="ID.00037">
       <bfo:content mcid="20" page="0">https://github.com/u-fischer/tagpdf</bfo:content>
       <bfo:annotation alt="url" index="1" page="0"/>
      </pdf2:Link>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
   </pdf2:Div>

  </TOC>
  <pdf2:Sect id="ID.00307">
   <ns3:section id="ID.00308">
    <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00309">
     <bfo:content mcid="14" page="2">1 </bfo:content>
    </pdf2:Lbl>
    <bfo:content mcid="15" page="2">Introduction</bfo:content>
   </ns3:section>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00310">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00311">
     <bfo:content mcid="16" page="2">Since many years the creation of accessible PDF-files with </bfo:content>
     <pdf2:Span ActualText="LaTeX" id="ID.00312">
      <bfo:content mcid="17" page="2">LATEX</bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Span>
     <bfo:content mcid="18" page="2"> which conform to the PDF/UA standard has been on the agenda of </bfo:content>
     <pdf2:Span ActualText="TeX" id="ID.00313">
      <bfo:content mcid="19" page="2">TEX</bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Span>
     <bfo:content mcid="20" page="2">-meetings. Many people agree that this is important and Ross Moore has done quite some work on it. There is also a TUG-mailing list and a webpage [5] dedicated to this theme.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00314">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00315">
     <bfo:content mcid="21" page="2">But in my opinion missing were means to </bfo:content>
     <pdf2:Em id="ID.00316">
      <bfo:content mcid="22" page="2">experiment</bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Em>
     <bfo:content mcid="23" page="2"> with tagging and accessibility. Means to try out, how difficult it is to tag some structures, means to try out, how much tagging is really needed (standards and validators donâ€™t need to be right â€¦), means to test what else is needed so that a PDF works e.g. with a screen reader. Without such experiments it is imho quite difficult to get a feeling about what has to be done, which kernel changes are needed, how packages should be adapted.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00317">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00318">
     <bfo:content mcid="24" page="2">This package were developped to close this gap by offering </bfo:content>
     <pdf2:Em id="ID.00319">
      <bfo:content mcid="25" page="2">core</bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Em>
     <bfo:content mcid="26" page="2"> commands to tag a PDF</bfo:content>
     <ns3:footnotemark id="ID.00320" ref="[ID.00322]">
      <pdf2:Link id="ID.00321">
       <bfo:content mcid="27" page="2">2</bfo:content>
       <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="4" page="2"/>
      </pdf2:Link>
     </ns3:footnotemark>
     <ns3:footnote id="ID.00322" ref="[ID.00320]">
      <ns3:footnotelabel id="ID.00323">
       <pdf2:NonStruct id="ID.00326">
        <bfo:content mcid="47" page="2">2</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:NonStruct>
      </ns3:footnotelabel>
      <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00324">
       <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00325">
        <bfo:content mcid="48" page="2">In case you donâ€™t know what this means: there will be some explanations later on.</bfo:content>
       </ns3:text>
      </ns3:text-unit>
     </ns3:footnote>
     <bfo:content mcid="28" page="2">. My hope was that the knowledge gained by the use of this package will at the end allow to decide if and how code to do tagging should be part of the </bfo:content>
     <pdf2:Span ActualText="LaTeX" id="ID.00327">
      <bfo:content mcid="29" page="2">LATEX</bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Span>
     <bfo:content mcid="30" page="2"> kernel.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00328">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00329">
     <bfo:content mcid="31" page="2">The code has been written with the goal to extend </bfo:content>
     <pdf2:Span ActualText="LaTeX" id="ID.00330">
      <bfo:content mcid="32" page="2">LATEX</bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Span>
     <bfo:content mcid="33" page="2"> itself. It therefore quite does not patch commands from other packages and is also not an aim of the package to develop such patches. While at the end changes to various commands in many classes and packages will be needed to get tagged PDF files â€“ and the examples accompanying the package try (or will try) to show various strategies â€“ these changes should in my opinion be done by the class, package and document writers themselves using a sensible API provided by the kernel and not by some external package that adds patches everywhere and would need constant maintenance â€“ one only need to look at packages like tex4ht or bidi or hyperref to see how difficult and sometimes fragile this is.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00331">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00332">
     <bfo:content mcid="34" page="2">The package is now a part of the Tagged PDF project and triggered already various changes in the LaTeX kernel and the engines: There is a new PDF management, the new para hooks allows to automatically tag paragraphs, after changes in the output routine page breaks and header and footer are handled correctly, the engines support now structure destinations.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00333">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00334">
     <bfo:content mcid="35" page="2">Iâ€™m sure that it still has bugs. Bugs reports, suggestions and comments can be added to the issue tracker on github. </bfo:content>
     <pdf2:Link id="ID.00335">
      <bfo:content mcid="36" page="2">https://github.com/u-fischer/tagpdf</bfo:content>
      <bfo:annotation alt="url" index="5" page="2"/>
     </pdf2:Link>
     <bfo:content mcid="37" page="2">.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00336">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00337">
     <bfo:content mcid="38" page="2">Please also check the github site for new examples and improvements.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <pdf2:Sect id="ID.00338">
    <ns3:subsection id="ID.00339">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00340">
      <bfo:content mcid="39" page="2">1.1 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="40" page="2">Tagging and accessibility</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00341">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00342">
      <bfo:content mcid="41" page="2">While the package is named tagpdf the goal is actually </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Em id="ID.00343">
       <bfo:content mcid="42" page="2">accessible</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Em>
      <bfo:content mcid="43" page="2"> PDF-files. Tagging is </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Em id="ID.00344">
       <bfo:content mcid="44" page="2">one</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Em>
      <bfo:content mcid="45" page="2">requirement for accessibility but there are others. I will mention some later on in this docu-mentation, and â€“ if sensible â€“ I will also try to add code, keys or tips for them.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00345">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00346">
      <bfo:content mcid="46" page="2">So the name of the package is a bit wrong. As excuse I can only say that it is shorter and easier to pronounce.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
   </pdf2:Sect>
   <pdf2:Sect id="ID.00347">
    <ns3:subsection id="ID.00348">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00349">
      <bfo:content mcid="0" page="3">1.2 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="1" page="3">Engines and modes</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00350">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00351">
      <bfo:content mcid="2" page="3">The package theoretically with all engines, But the xelatex and the latex-dvips-route are not much tested and they also donâ€™t support real space glyphs. lualatex is the most powerful and safe modus, but pdflatex works ok too.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00352">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00353">
      <bfo:content mcid="3" page="3">The package has two modes: the </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Em id="ID.00354">
       <bfo:content mcid="4" page="3">generic mode</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Em>
      <bfo:content mcid="5" page="3"> which should work in theory with every engine and the </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Em id="ID.00355">
       <bfo:content mcid="6" page="3">lua mode</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Em>
      <bfo:content mcid="7" page="3"> which works only with lualatex.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00356">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00357">
      <bfo:content mcid="8" page="3">I implemented the generic mode first. Mostly because my tex skills are much better than my lua skills and I wanted to get the tex side right before starting to fight with attributes and node traversing.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00358">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00359">
      <bfo:content mcid="9" page="3">While the generic mode is not bad and I spent quite some time to get it working I nevertheless think that the lua mode is the future and the only one that will be usable for larger documents. PDF is a page orientated format and so the ability of luatex to manipulate pages and nodes after the </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Span ActualText="TeX" id="ID.00360">
       <bfo:content mcid="10" page="3">TEX</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Span>
      <bfo:content mcid="11" page="3">-processing is really useful here. Also with luatex characters are normally already given as unicode.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00361">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00362">
      <bfo:content mcid="12" page="3">The package uses quite a lot labels (in generic mode more than with luamode). At the begin it relied on the zref package, but switched now to a new experimental implementation for labels. The drawback of the new method is that they donâ€™t give yet good rerun messages if they have changed. I advise to use the rerunfilecheck package as a intermediate work-around and when using pdflatex compile at best at least once or twice more often then normal.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
   </pdf2:Sect>
   <pdf2:Sect id="ID.00363">
    <ns3:subsection id="ID.00364">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00365">
      <bfo:content mcid="13" page="3">1.3 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="14" page="3">References and target PDF version</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00366">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00367">
      <bfo:content mcid="15" page="3">My main reference for the first versions of this package was the free reference for PDF 1.7. [2] and so the package also targetted this version.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00368">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00369">
      <bfo:content mcid="16" page="3">In 2018 PDF 2.0. has been released, and since 2020 all engines can set the version to 2.0. So the package will now target PDF 2.0. This doesnâ€™t mean that 2.0 will be required, but that the code and the options will be extended to support PDF 2.0. One example is the support for associated files, another the support for name spaces in version 0.82.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00370">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00371">
      <bfo:content mcid="17" page="3">The package doesnâ€™t try to suppress all 2.0 features if an older PDF version is produced. It normally doesnâ€™t harm if a PDF contains keys unknown in its version and it makes the code faster and easier to maintain if there arenâ€™t too many tests and code pathes; so for example associated files will always be added. But tests could be added in case this leads to incompabilities.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00372">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00373">
      <bfo:content mcid="18" page="3">It should be noted that some tools donâ€™t like PDF 2.0. PAC 3 for example simply crashes, and pdftk will create a PDF 1.0 from it. This makes testing PDF 2.0 files a bit of a challenge.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
   </pdf2:Sect>
   <pdf2:Sect id="ID.00374">
    <ns3:subsection id="ID.00375">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00376">
      <bfo:content mcid="19" page="3">1.4 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="20" page="3">Validation</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00377">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00378">
      <bfo:content mcid="21" page="3">PDFâ€™s created with the commands of this package must be validated:</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00379">
     <ns3:itemize class="itemize" id="ID.00380">
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.00381">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00382">
        <bfo:content mcid="22" page="3">â€¢</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.00383">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00384">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00385">
          <bfo:content mcid="23" page="3">One must check that the PDF is </bfo:content>
          <pdf2:Em id="ID.00386">
           <bfo:content mcid="24" page="3">syntactically</bfo:content>
          </pdf2:Em>
          <bfo:content mcid="25" page="3"> correct. It is rather easy to create broken PDF: e.g. if a chunk is opened on one page but closed on the next page or if the document isnâ€™t compiled often enough.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.00387">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00388">
        <bfo:content mcid="26" page="3">â€¢</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.00389">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00390">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00391">
          <bfo:content mcid="27" page="3">One must check how good the requirements of the PDF/UA standard are followed </bfo:content>
          <pdf2:Em id="ID.00392">
           <bfo:content mcid="28" page="3">for-mally</bfo:content>
          </pdf2:Em>
          <bfo:content mcid="29" page="3">.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.00393">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00394">
        <bfo:content mcid="30" page="3">â€¢</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.00395">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00396">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00397">
          <bfo:content mcid="31" page="3">One must check how good the accessibility is </bfo:content>
          <pdf2:Em id="ID.00398">
           <bfo:content mcid="32" page="3">practically</bfo:content>
          </pdf2:Em>
          <bfo:content mcid="33" page="3">.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
     </ns3:itemize>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00399">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00400">
      <bfo:content mcid="0" page="4">Syntax validation and formal standard validation can be done with preflight of the (non-free) adobe acrobat. It can also be done also with the free PDF Accessibility Checker (PAC 3) [7]. There is also the validator veraPDF [6]. A rather new and quite useful tool is â€œNext Generation PDFâ€ [3], a browser application which converts a tagged PDF to html, allows to inspect its structure and also to edit the structure.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00401">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00402">
      <bfo:content mcid="1" page="4">Practical validation is naturally the more complicated part. It needs screen reader, users which actually knows how to handle them, can test documents and can report where a PDF has real accessibility problems.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00403">
     <pdf2:H10 class="raggedright" id="ID.00404">
      <bfo:content mcid="2" page="4">Preflight woes</bfo:content>
     </pdf2:H10>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00405">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00406">
      <bfo:content mcid="3" page="4">Sadly validators can not be always trusted. As an example for an reason that I donâ€™t understand the adobe preflight donâ€™t like the list structure L. It is also possible that validators contradict: that the one says everything is okay, while the other complains.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
   </pdf2:Sect>
   <pdf2:Sect id="ID.00407">
    <ns3:subsection id="ID.00408">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00409">
      <bfo:content mcid="4" page="4">1.5 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="5" page="4">Examples wanted!</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00410">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00411">
      <bfo:content mcid="6" page="4">To make the package usable examples are needed: examples that demonstrate how various structures can be tagged and which patches are needed, examples for the test suite, examples that demonstrates problems.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <pdf2:Div id="ID.00412"/>
    <pdf2:Div id="ID.00413">
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00414">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00415">
       <bfo:content mcid="7" page="4">Feedback, contribuations and corrections are welcome!</bfo:content>

     </ns3:text>

   <pdf2:Sect id="ID.00422">
    <ns3:subsection id="ID.00423">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00424">
      <bfo:content mcid="11" page="4">2.1 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="12" page="4">Changes in 0.3</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00425">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00426">
      <bfo:content mcid="13" page="4">In this version I improved the handling of alternative and actual text. See section </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Link id="ID.00427">
       <bfo:content mcid="14" page="4">5</bfo:content>
       <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="0" page="4"/>
      </pdf2:Link>

    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00428">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00429">

     </ns3:text>

   </pdf2:Sect>
   <pdf2:Sect id="ID.00430">
    <ns3:subsection id="ID.00431">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00432">
      <bfo:content mcid="17" page="4">2.2 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="18" page="4">Changes in 0.5</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00433">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00434">
      <bfo:content mcid="19" page="4">I added code to handle attributes and attribute classes, see section </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Link id="ID.00435">
       <bfo:content mcid="20" page="4">4.3.5</bfo:content>

    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00436">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00437">
      <bfo:content mcid="22" page="4">I added code to add â€œrealâ€ space glyphs to the PDF, see section </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Link id="ID.00438">
       <bfo:content mcid="23" page="4">8</bfo:content>
       <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="2" page="4"/>
      </pdf2:Link>
      <bfo:content mcid="24" page="4">.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
   </pdf2:Sect>
   <pdf2:Sect id="ID.00439">
    <ns3:subsection id="ID.00440">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00441">
      <bfo:content mcid="25" page="4">2.3 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="26" page="4">Changes in 0.6</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00442">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00443">
      <pdf2:Strong id="ID.00444">
       <bfo:content mcid="27" page="4">Breaking change!</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Strong>
      <bfo:content mcid="28" page="4"> The attributes used in luamode to mark the MC-chunks are no longer set globally. I thought that global attributes would make it easier to tag, but it only leads to problem when e.g. header and footer are inserted. So from this version on the attributes are set locally and the effect of a \tagmcbegin ends with the current group. This means that in some cases more \tagmcbegin are needed and this affected some of the examples, e.g. the patching </bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="0" page="5">commands for sections with KOMA. On the other side it means that quite often one can omit the \tagmcend command.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
   </pdf2:Sect>

     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="28" page="8">Proof of concept: the tagging of the documentation itself</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00772">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00773">
      <bfo:content mcid="29" page="8">Starting with version 0.6 the documentation itself has been tagged. The tagging wasnâ€™t (and isnâ€™t) in no way perfect. The validator from Adobe didnâ€™t complain, but PAC 3 wanted alternative text for all links (no idea why) and so I put everywhere simple text like â€œ linkâ€ and â€œrefâ€. The links to footnotes gave warnings, so I disabled them. I used types from the PDF version 1.7, mostly as I had no idea what should be used for code in 2.0. Margin notes were simply wrong â€¦</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00774">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00775">
      <bfo:content mcid="30" page="8">The tagging has been improved and automated over time in sync with improvements and new features in the LaTeX kernel and the PDF management code and is now much better. Sadly the output of the validators donâ€™t quite reflect the improvements. The documentation uses now PDF 2.0 and PAC 3 canâ€™t handle this, it claims that the file is damaged. The Adobe validator has a bug and doesnâ€™t like the (valid) use of the Lbl tag for the section numbers (see figure </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Link id="ID.00776">
       <bfo:content mcid="31" page="8">1</bfo:content>
       <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="3" page="8"/>
      </pdf2:Link>
      <bfo:content mcid="32" page="8">).</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00777">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00778">
      <bfo:content mcid="33" page="8">But even if the documentation passed the tests of the validators: as mentioned above passing a formal test doesnâ€™t mean that the content is really good and usable. I have a lot doubts that the code parts are really readable. The bibliography and the references must be improved. The user commands used for the tagging and also some of the patches used are still rather crude. So there is lot space for improvement.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>

   <ns3:section id="ID.00794">
    <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00795">
     <bfo:content mcid="2" page="9">3 </bfo:content>
    </pdf2:Lbl>
    <bfo:content mcid="3" page="9">Loading</bfo:content>
   </ns3:section>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00796">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00797">
     <bfo:content mcid="4" page="9">The package requires the new PDF management. With a current </bfo:content>
     <pdf2:Span ActualText="LaTeX" id="ID.00798">
      <bfo:content mcid="5" page="9">LATEX</bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Span>
     <bfo:content mcid="6" page="9"> (2022-06-01 or newer) the PDF management is loaded if you use the \DocumentMetadata command before \documentclass. The tagpdf package can then be loaded and activated by using the testphase key. The exact behaviour of the testphase key is documented in documentmetadata-support-doc.pdf which is part of the latex-lab bundle.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00799">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00800">
     <bfo:content mcid="7" page="9">Various parts of the code differentiate between PDF version 2.0 and lower versions. If PDF 2.0 is wanted it is required to set the version early in the \DocumentMetadata command so thattagpdf can pick up the correct code path.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00801">
    <ns6:verbatim id="ID.00802">
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.00803">

   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00825">
    <pdf2:H10 class="raggedright" id="ID.00826">
     <bfo:content mcid="6" page="10">Deactivation</bfo:content>
    </pdf2:H10>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00827">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00828">
     <bfo:content mcid="7" page="10">When loading tagpdf through the testphase keys, it is automatically activated. To deactivate it while still retaining all the other new code from the latex-lab testphase files, use in the preamble \tagpdfsetup{activate-all=false}. You can additionally also deactivate the paratagging and the interword space code. To suppress the loading of the package alltogether you can try</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00829">
    <ns6:verbatim id="ID.00830">
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.00831">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.00832">
       <bfo:content mcid="8" page="10">\makeatletter</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.00833">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.00834">
       <bfo:content mcid="9" page="10">\disable@package@load{tagpdf}{}</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.00835">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.00836">
       <bfo:content mcid="10" page="10">\makeatother</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.00837">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.00838">
       <bfo:content mcid="11" page="10">\DocumentMetadata{...}</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
    </ns6:verbatim>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00839">
    <pdf2:H10 class="raggedright" id="ID.00840">
     <bfo:content mcid="12" page="10">Loading as package needs activation!</bfo:content>
    </pdf2:H10>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00841">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00842">
     <bfo:content mcid="13" page="10">It is not recommended anymore, but the package can also be loaded normally with \usepackage (but it is still required to use \DocumentMetadata to load the PDF management) but it will then â€“ apart from loading more packages and defining a lot of things â€“ not do much. You will have to </bfo:content>
     <pdf2:Em id="ID.00843">
      <bfo:content mcid="14" page="10">activate</bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Em>
     <bfo:content mcid="15" page="10"> it with \tagpdfsetup.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00844">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00845">
     <bfo:content mcid="16" page="10">The PDF management loaded with \DocumentMetadata will in any case load tagpdf-base a small package that provides no-op versions of the main tagging commands.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00846">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00847">
     <bfo:content mcid="17" page="10">Most commands do nothing if tagging is not activated, but in case a test is needed a com-mand (with the usual p,T,F variants) is provided:</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <Code id="ID.00848">
    <bfo:content mcid="18" page="10"/>
    <bfo:content mcid="19" page="10">\tag_if_active:TF</bfo:content>
    <bfo:content mcid="20" page="10"/>
   </Code>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00849">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00850">
     <bfo:content mcid="21" page="10">The check is true only if </bfo:content>
     <pdf2:Em id="ID.00851">
      <bfo:content mcid="22" page="10">everything</bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Em>
     <bfo:content mcid="23" page="10"> is activated. In all other cases (including if tagging has been stopped locally) it will be false.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <pdf2:Sect id="ID.00852">
    <ns3:subsection id="ID.00853">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00854">
      <bfo:content mcid="0" page="11">3.1 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="1" page="11">Modes and package options</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00855">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00856">
      <bfo:content mcid="2" page="11">The package has two different modes: The</bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Strong id="ID.00857">
       <bfo:content mcid="3" page="11"> generic mode</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Strong>
      <bfo:content mcid="4" page="11"> works (in theory, currently only fully tested with pdflatex) probably with all engines, the</bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Strong id="ID.00858">
       <bfo:content mcid="5" page="11"> lua mode</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Strong>
      <bfo:content mcid="6" page="11"> only with lualatex. The differences between both modes will be described later. The mode can be set with package options:</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00859">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00860">
      <bfo:content mcid="7" page="11">luamode</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00861">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00862">
      <bfo:content mcid="8" page="11">This is the default mode. It will use the generic mode if the document is processed with pdflatex and the lua mode with lualatex.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00863">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00864">
      <bfo:content mcid="9" page="11">genericmode</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00865">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00866">
      <bfo:content mcid="10" page="11">This will force the generic mode for all engines.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
   </pdf2:Sect>
   <pdf2:Sect id="ID.00867">
    <ns3:subsection id="ID.00868">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00869">
      <bfo:content mcid="11" page="11">3.2 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="12" page="11">Setup and activation</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <Code id="ID.00870">
     <bfo:content mcid="13" page="11"/>
     <bfo:content mcid="14" page="11">\tagpdfsetup{âŸ¨key-val-listâŸ©}</bfo:content>
     <bfo:content mcid="15" page="11"/>
    </Code>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00871">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00872">
      <bfo:content mcid="16" page="11">This command setups the general behaviour of the package. The command should be normally used only in the preamble (for a few keys it could also make sense to change them in the document).</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00873">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00874">
      <bfo:content mcid="17" page="11">The key-val list understands the following keys:</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00875">
     <ns3:description class="description" id="ID.00876">
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.00877">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00878">
        <bfo:content mcid="18" page="11">activate-all</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.00879">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00880">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00881">
          <bfo:content mcid="19" page="11">Boolean, initially false. Activates everything, thatâ€™s normally the sensible thing to do.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.00882">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00883">
        <bfo:content mcid="20" page="11">activate</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.00884">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00885">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00886">
          <bfo:content mcid="21" page="11">Like activate-all, </bfo:content>
          <pdf2:Em id="ID.00887">
           <bfo:content mcid="22" page="11">additionally</bfo:content>
          </pdf2:Em>
          <bfo:content mcid="23" page="11"> is opens at begin document a structure with \tagstructbegin and closes it at end document. The key accepts as value a tag name which is used as the tag of the structure. The default value is Document.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>

      </pdf2:LI>

      <pdf2:LI id="ID.00937">

       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.00955">
