Perhaps this should be changed â€¦.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.00960">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00961">
        <bfo:content mcid="17" page="12">tagunmarked</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.00962">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00963">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00964">
          <bfo:content mcid="18" page="12">Boolean,</bfo:content>
          <bfo:content mcid="19" page="12"> initially true. When this boolean is true, the lua code will try to mark everything that has not been marked yet as an artifact. The benefit is that one doesnâ€™t have to mark up every deco rule oneself. The danger is that it perhaps marks things that shouldnâ€™t be marked â€“ it hasnâ€™t been tested yet with complicated documents containing annotations etc. See also section </bfo:content>
          <pdf2:Link id="ID.00965">
           <bfo:content mcid="20" page="12">4.7</bfo:content>
           <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="1" page="12"/>
          </pdf2:Link>
          <bfo:content mcid="21" page="12"> for a discussion about automatic tagging.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.00966">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00967">
        <bfo:content mcid="22" page="12">uncompress</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.00968">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00969">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00970">
          <bfo:content mcid="23" page="12">Sets both the PDF compresslevel and the PDF objcompresslevel to 0 and so allows to inspect the PDF.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
     </ns3:description>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <Code id="ID.00971">
     <bfo:content mcid="24" page="12"/>
     <bfo:content mcid="25" page="12">\tagtool{âŸ¨key-valâŸ©}</bfo:content>
     <bfo:content mcid="26" page="12"/>
    </Code>
    <Code id="ID.00972">
     <bfo:content mcid="27" page="12"/>
     <bfo:content mcid="28" page="12">\tag_tool:n{âŸ¨key-valâŸ©}</bfo:content>
     <bfo:content mcid="29" page="12"/>
    </Code>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00973">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00974">
      <bfo:content mcid="30" page="12">The tagging of document elements require a variety of small commands. This command will unify them under a common interface. This is work-in-progress and syntax and implementation can change! While the argument looks like a key-val </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Em id="ID.00975">
       <bfo:content mcid="31" page="12">list</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Em>
      <bfo:content mcid="32" page="12"> (and currently is actually one), this should not be relied on. Instead only one argument should be used as the implementation will change to improve the speed. Currently the following arguments are supported</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00976">
     <ns3:description class="description" id="ID.00977">
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.00978">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00979">
        <bfo:content mcid="33" page="12">para</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.00980">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00981">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00982">
          <bfo:content mcid="34" page="12">Boolean. It will replace the \tagpdfparaOn and \tagpdfparaOff command.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.00983">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00984">
        <bfo:content mcid="35" page="12">unittag</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.00985">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00986">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00987">
          <bfo:content mcid="36" page="12">String. It allows to change the outer tag used in the following automatically tagged paragraphs. The setting is local.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.00988">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00989">
        <bfo:content mcid="37" page="12">paratag</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.00990">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00991">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00992">
          <bfo:content mcid="38" page="12">String. It allows to change the inner tag used in the following automatically tagged paragraphs. The setting is local.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.00993">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.00994">
        <bfo:content mcid="39" page="12">para-flattened</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.00995">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.00996">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.00997">
          <bfo:content mcid="40" page="12">Boolean. If set it will suppress the outer structure in the automatic paratagging. This should be applied to the start and end hook in the same way! The setting is local.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
     </ns3:description>
    </ns3:text-unit>
   </pdf2:Sect>
  </pdf2:Sect>
  <pdf2:Sect id="ID.00998">
   <ns3:section id="ID.00999">
    <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01000">
     <bfo:content mcid="0" page="13">4 </bfo:content>
    </pdf2:Lbl>
    <bfo:content mcid="1" page="13">Tagging</bfo:content>
   </ns3:section>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01001">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01002">
     <bfo:content mcid="2" page="13">pdf is a page orientated graphic format. It simply puts ink and glyphs at various coordinates on a page. A simple stream of a page can look like this</bfo:content>
     <ns3:footnotemark id="ID.01003" ref="[ID.01005]">
      <pdf2:Link id="ID.01004">
       <bfo:content mcid="3" page="13">3</bfo:content>
       <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="0" page="13"/>
      </pdf2:Link>
     </ns3:footnotemark>
     <ns3:footnote id="ID.01005" ref="[ID.01003]">
      <ns3:footnotelabel id="ID.01006">
       <pdf2:NonStruct id="ID.01009">
        <bfo:content mcid="36" page="13">3</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:NonStruct>
      </ns3:footnotelabel>
      <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01007">
       <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01008">
        <bfo:content mcid="37" page="13">The appendix contains some remarks about the syntax of a PDF file</bfo:content>
       </ns3:text>
      </ns3:text-unit>
     </ns3:footnote>
     <bfo:content mcid="4" page="13">:</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01010">
    <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01011">
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.01012">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.01013">
       <bfo:content mcid="5" page="13">stream</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.01014">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.01015">
       <bfo:content mcid="6" page="13">   BT</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.01016">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.01017">
       <bfo:content mcid="7" page="13">   /F27 14.3462 Tf                 %select font</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.01018">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.01019">
       <bfo:content mcid="8" page="13">   89.291 746.742 Td               %move point</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.01020">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.01021">
       <bfo:content mcid="9" page="13">   [(1)-574(Intro)-32(duction)]TJ  %print text</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.01022">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.01023">
       <bfo:content mcid="10" page="13">   /F24 10.9091 Tf                 %select font</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.01024">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.01025">
       <bfo:content mcid="11" page="13">    0 -24.35 Td                    %move point</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.01026">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.01027">
       <bfo:content mcid="12" page="13">    [(Let's)-331(start)]TJ         %print text</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.01028">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.01029">
       <bfo:content mcid="13" page="13">    205.635 -605.688 Td            %move point</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.01030">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.01031">
       <bfo:content mcid="14" page="13">    [(1)]TJ                        %print text</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.01032">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.01033">
       <bfo:content mcid="15" page="13">   ET</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.01034">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.01035">
       <bfo:content mcid="16" page="13">endstream</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
    </ns6:verbatim>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01036">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01037">
     <bfo:content mcid="17" page="13">From this stream one can extract the characters and their placement on the page but not their semantic meaning (the first line is actually a section heading, the last the page number). And while in the example the order is correct there is actually no guaranty that the stream contains the text in the order it should be read.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01038">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01039">
     <bfo:content mcid="18" page="13">Tagging means to enrich the PDF with information about the </bfo:content>
     <pdf2:Em id="ID.01040">
      <bfo:content mcid="19" page="13">semantic</bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Em>
     <bfo:content mcid="20" page="13"> meaning and the </bfo:content>
     <pdf2:Em id="ID.01041">
      <bfo:content mcid="21" page="13">reading order</bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Em>
     <bfo:content mcid="22" page="13">. (Tagging can do more, one can also store all sorts of layout information like font properties and indentation with tags. But as I already wrote this package concentrates on the part of tagging that is needed to improve accessibility.)</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01042">
    <ns3:subsection id="ID.01043">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01044">
      <bfo:content mcid="23" page="13">4.1 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="24" page="13">Three tasks</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01045">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01046">
      <bfo:content mcid="25" page="13">To tag a PDF three tasks must be carried out:</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01047">
     <ns3:enumerate class="enumerate" id="ID.01048">
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.01049">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01050">
        <bfo:content mcid="26" page="13">1.</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01051">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01052">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01053">
          <pdf2:Strong id="ID.01054">
           <bfo:content mcid="27" page="13">The mark-content-task</bfo:content>
          </pdf2:Strong>
          <bfo:content mcid="28" page="13">:</bfo:content>
          <bfo:content mcid="29" page="13"> The document must add â€œ labelsâ€ to the page stream which allows to identify and reference the various chunks of text and other content. This is the most difficult part of tagging â€“ both for the document writer but also for the package code. At first there can be quite many chunks as every one is a leaf node of the structure and so often a rather small unit. At second the chunks must be defined page-wise â€“ and this is not easy when you donâ€™t know where the page breaks are. Also in a standard document a lot text is created automatically, e.g. the toc, references, citations, list numbers etc and it is not always easy to mark them correctly.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.01055">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01056">
        <bfo:content mcid="30" page="13">2.</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01057">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01058">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01059">
          <pdf2:Strong id="ID.01060">
           <bfo:content mcid="31" page="13">The structure-task</bfo:content>
          </pdf2:Strong>
          <bfo:content mcid="32" page="13">:</bfo:content>
          <bfo:content mcid="33" page="13"> The document must declare the structure. This means marking the start and end of semantically connected portions of the document (correctly nested as a tree). This too means some work for the document writer, but less than for the mc-task: at first quite often the mc-task and the structure-task can be combined, e.g. when you mark up a list number or a tabular cell or a section header; at second one doesnâ€™t have to worry about page breaks so quite often one can patch standard environments to declare the structure. On the other side a number of structures end in </bfo:content>
          <pdf2:Span ActualText="LaTeX" id="ID.01061">
           <bfo:content mcid="34" page="13">LATEX</bfo:content>
          </pdf2:Span>
          <bfo:content mcid="35" page="13"> only implicitly â€“ e.g. an item ends at the next item, so getting the PDF structure right still means that additional mark up must be added.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.01062">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01063">
        <bfo:content mcid="6" page="14">3.</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01064">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01065">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01066">
          <pdf2:Strong id="ID.01067">
           <bfo:content mcid="7" page="14">The tree management</bfo:content>
          </pdf2:Strong>
          <bfo:content mcid="8" page="14">:</bfo:content>
          <bfo:content mcid="9" page="14"> At last the structure must be written into the PDF. For every structure an object of type StructElem must be created and flushed with keys for the parents and the kids. A parenttree must be created to get a reference from the mc-chunks to the parent structure. A rolemap must be written. And a number of dictionary entries. All this is hopefully done automatically and correctly by the package â€¦.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
     </ns3:enumerate>
    </ns3:text-unit>
   </pdf2:Sect>
   <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01080">
    <ns3:subsection id="ID.01081">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01082">
      <bfo:content mcid="10" page="14">4.2 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="11" page="14">Task 1: Marking the chunks: the mark-content-step</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01083">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01084">
      <bfo:content mcid="12" page="14">To be able to refer to parts of the text in the structure, the text in the page stream must get â€œ labelsâ€. In the PDF reference they are called â€œmarked contentâ€. The three main variants needed here are:</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01085">
     <ns3:description class="description" id="ID.01086">
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.01087">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01088">
        <bfo:content mcid="13" page="14">Artifacts</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01089">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01090">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01091">
          <bfo:content mcid="14" page="14">They are marked with of a pair of keywords, BMC and EMC which surrounds the text.BMC has a single prefix argument, the fix tag name /Artifact. Artifacts should be used for irrelevant text and page content that should be ignored in the structure. Sadly it is often not possible to leave such text simply unmarked â€“ the accessibility tests in Acrobat and other validators complain.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01092">
         <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01093">
          <ns6:codeline id="ID.01094">
           <Code class="justify" id="ID.01095">
            <bfo:content mcid="0" page="15">/Artifact BMC</bfo:content>
           </Code>
          </ns6:codeline>
          <ns6:codeline id="ID.01096">
           <Code class="justify" id="ID.01097">
            <bfo:content mcid="1" page="15"> text to be marked</bfo:content>
           </Code>
          </ns6:codeline>
          <ns6:codeline id="ID.01098">
           <Code class="justify" id="ID.01099">
            <bfo:content mcid="2" page="15">/EMC</bfo:content>
           </Code>
          </ns6:codeline>
         </ns6:verbatim>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.01100">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01101">
        <bfo:content mcid="3" page="15">Artifacts with a type</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01102">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01103">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01104">
          <bfo:content mcid="4" page="15">They are marked with of a pair of keywords, BDC and EMC which surrounds the text. BDC has two arguments: again the tag name /Artifact and a following dictionary which allows to specify the suppressed info. Text in header and footer can e.g. be declared as pagination like this:</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01105">
         <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01106">
          <ns6:codeline id="ID.01107">
           <Code class="justify" id="ID.01108">
            <bfo:content mcid="5" page="15">/Artifact &lt;&lt;/Type /Pagination&gt;&gt; BDC</bfo:content>
           </Code>
          </ns6:codeline>
          <ns6:codeline id="ID.01109">
           <Code class="justify" id="ID.01110">
            <bfo:content mcid="6" page="15"> text to be marked</bfo:content>
           </Code>
          </ns6:codeline>
          <ns6:codeline id="ID.01111">
           <Code class="justify" id="ID.01112">
            <bfo:content mcid="7" page="15">/EMC</bfo:content>
           </Code>
          </ns6:codeline>
         </ns6:verbatim>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.01113">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01114">
        <bfo:content mcid="8" page="15">Content</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01115">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01116">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01117">
          <bfo:content mcid="9" page="15">Content is marked also with of a pair of keywords, BDC and EMC. The first argument of BDC is a tag name which describes the structural type of the text</bfo:content>
          <ns3:footnotemark id="ID.01118" ref="[ID.01120]">
           <pdf2:Link id="ID.01119">
            <bfo:content mcid="10" page="15">4</bfo:content>
            <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="0" page="15"/>
           </pdf2:Link>
          </ns3:footnotemark>
          <ns3:footnote id="ID.01120" ref="[ID.01118]">
           <ns3:footnotelabel id="ID.01121">
            <pdf2:NonStruct id="ID.01124">
             <bfo:content mcid="27" page="15">4</bfo:content>
            </pdf2:NonStruct>
           </ns3:footnotelabel>
           <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01122">
            <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01123">
             <bfo:content mcid="28" page="15">There is quite some redundancy in the specification here. The structural type is also set in the structure tree. One wonders if it isnâ€™t enough to use always /SPAN here.</bfo:content>
            </ns3:text>
           </ns3:text-unit>
          </ns3:footnote>
          <bfo:content mcid="11" page="15"> Examples are /P(paragraph), /H2 (heading), /TD (table cell). The reference mentions a number of standard types but it is possible to add more or to use different names.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01125">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01126">
          <bfo:content mcid="12" page="15">In the second argument of BDC â€“ in the property dictionary â€“ more data can be stored. </bfo:content>
          <pdf2:Em id="ID.01127">
           <bfo:content mcid="13" page="15">Required</bfo:content>
          </pdf2:Em>
          <bfo:content mcid="14" page="15"> is an /MCID-key which takes an integer as a value:</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01128">
         <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01129">
          <ns6:codeline id="ID.01130">
           <Code class="justify" id="ID.01131">
            <bfo:content mcid="15" page="15">/H1 &lt;&lt;/MCID 3&gt;&gt; BDC</bfo:content>
           </Code>
          </ns6:codeline>
          <ns6:codeline id="ID.01132">
           <Code class="justify" id="ID.01133">
            <bfo:content mcid="16" page="15"> text to be marked</bfo:content>
           </Code>
          </ns6:codeline>
          <ns6:codeline id="ID.01134">
           <Code class="justify" id="ID.01135">
            <bfo:content mcid="17" page="15">/EMC</bfo:content>
           </Code>
          </ns6:codeline>
         </ns6:verbatim>
        </ns3:text-unit>
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01136">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01137">
          <bfo:content mcid="18" page="15">This integer is used to identify the chunk when building the structure tree. The chunks are numbered by page starting with 0. As the numbers are also used as an index in an array they shouldnâ€™t be â€œ holesâ€ in the numbering system (It is perhaps possible to handle a numbering scheme not starting by 0 and having holes, but it will enlarge the PDF as one would need dummy objects.).</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01138">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01139">
          <bfo:content mcid="19" page="15">It is possible to add more entries to the property dictionary, e.g. a title, alternative text or a local language setting.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
     </ns3:description>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01140">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01141">
      <bfo:content mcid="20" page="15">The needed markers can be added with low level code e.g. like this (in pdftex syntax):</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01142">
     <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01143">
      <ns6:codeline id="ID.01144">
       <Code class="justify" id="ID.01145">
        <bfo:content mcid="21" page="15">\pdfliteral page {/H1 &lt;&lt;/MCID 3&gt;&gt; BDC}%</bfo:content>
       </Code>
      </ns6:codeline>
      <ns6:codeline id="ID.01146">
       <Code class="justify" id="ID.01147">
        <bfo:content mcid="22" page="15"> text to be marked</bfo:content>
       </Code>
      </ns6:codeline>
      <ns6:codeline id="ID.01148">
       <Code class="justify" id="ID.01149">
        <bfo:content mcid="23" page="15">\pdfliteral page {EMC}%</bfo:content>
       </Code>
      </ns6:codeline>
     </ns6:verbatim>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01150">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01151">
      <bfo:content mcid="24" page="15">This sounds easy. But there are quite a number of traps, mostly with pdfLaTeX:</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01152">
     <ns3:enumerate class="enumerate" id="ID.01153">
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.01154">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01155">
        <bfo:content mcid="25" page="15">1.</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01156">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01157">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01158">
          <bfo:content mcid="26" page="15">PDF is a page oriented format. And this means that the start BDC/BMC and the correspond-ing end EMC must be on the same page. So marking e.g. a section title like in the following example wonâ€™t always work as the literal before the section could end on the previous page:</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01159">
         <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01160">
          <ns6:codeline id="ID.01161">
           <Code class="justify" id="ID.01162">
            <bfo:content mcid="0" page="16">\pdfliteral page {/H1 &lt;&lt;/MCID 3&gt;&gt; BDC} %problem: possible pagebreak here</bfo:content>
           </Code>
          </ns6:codeline>
          <ns6:codeline id="ID.01163">
           <Code class="justify" id="ID.01164">
            <bfo:content mcid="1" page="16"> \section{mysection}</bfo:content>
           </Code>
          </ns6:codeline>
          <ns6:codeline id="ID.01165">
           <Code class="justify" id="ID.01166">
            <bfo:content mcid="2" page="16">\pdfliteral page {EMC}%</bfo:content>
           </Code>
          </ns6:codeline>
         </ns6:verbatim>
        </ns3:text-unit>
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01167">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01168">
          <bfo:content mcid="3" page="16">Using the literals </bfo:content>
          <pdf2:Em id="ID.01169">
           <bfo:content mcid="4" page="16">inside</bfo:content>
          </pdf2:Em>
          <bfo:content mcid="5" page="16"> the section argument is better, but then one has to take care that they donâ€™t wander into the header and the toc.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.01170">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01171">
        <bfo:content mcid="6" page="16">2.</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01172">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01173">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01174">
          <bfo:content mcid="7" page="16">Literals are â€œwhatsitsâ€ nodes and can change spacing, page and line breaking. The literal </bfo:content>
          <pdf2:Em id="ID.01175">
           <bfo:content mcid="8" page="16">behind</bfo:content>
          </pdf2:Em>
          <bfo:content mcid="9" page="16"> the section in the previous example could e.g. lead to a lonely section title at the end of the page.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.01176">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01177">
        <bfo:content mcid="10" page="16">3.</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01178">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01179">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01180">
          <bfo:content mcid="11" page="16">The /MCID numbers must be unique on a page. So you canâ€™t use the literal in a saved box that you reuse in various places. This is e.g. a problem with longtable as it saves the table header and footer in a box.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.01181">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01182">
        <bfo:content mcid="12" page="16">4.</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01183">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01184">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01185">
          <bfo:content mcid="13" page="16">The /MCID-chunks are leaf nodes in the structure tree, so they shouldnâ€™t be nested.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.01186">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01187">
        <bfo:content mcid="14" page="16">5.</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01188">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01189">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01190">
          <bfo:content mcid="15" page="16">Often text in a document is created automatically or moved around: entries in the table of contents, index, bibliography and more. To mark these text chunks correctly one has to analyze the code creating such content to find suitable places to inject the literals.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.01191">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01192">
        <bfo:content mcid="16" page="16">6.</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01193">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01194">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01195">
          <bfo:content mcid="17" page="16">The literals are inserted directly and not at shipout. This means that due to the asyn-chronous page breaking of </bfo:content>
          <pdf2:Span ActualText="TeX" id="ID.01196">
           <bfo:content mcid="18" page="16">TEX</bfo:content>
          </pdf2:Span>
          <bfo:content mcid="19" page="16"> the MCID-number can be wrong even if the counter is reset at every page. This package uses in generic mode a label-ref-system to get around this problem. This sadly means that often at least three compilations are needed until everything has settled down.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01197">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01198">
          <bfo:content mcid="20" page="16">It can actually be worse: If the text is changed after the MCID-numbers have been assigned, and a new mc-chunk is inserted in the middle of the page, then all the numbers have to be recalculated and that requires again a number of compilations until it really settles down again. Internal references are especially problematic here, as the first compilation typically creates a non-link ??, and only the second inserts the structure and the new mc. When the reference system in LaTeX will be extended, care will be taken to ensure that already the dummy text builds a chunk. Until then the advice is to first compile the document and resolve all cross-reference and to activate tagging only at the end.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.01199">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01200">
        <bfo:content mcid="21" page="16">7.</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01201">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01202">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01203">
          <bfo:content mcid="22" page="16">There exist environments which process their content more than once â€“ examples arealign and tabularx. So one has to check for doublettes and holes in the counting system.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
      <pdf2:LI id="ID.01204">
       <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01205">
        <bfo:content mcid="23" page="16">8.</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Lbl>
       <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01206">
        <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01207">
         <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01208">
          <bfo:content mcid="24" page="16">PDF is a page oriented format. And this means that the start and the end marker must be on the same page â€¦ </bfo:content>
          <pdf2:Em id="ID.01209">
           <bfo:content mcid="25" page="16">so what to do with normal paragraphs that split over pages??</bfo:content>
          </pdf2:Em>
          <bfo:content mcid="26" page="16">. This question will be discussed in subsection </bfo:content>
          <pdf2:Link id="ID.01210">
           <bfo:content mcid="27" page="16">4.2.9</bfo:content>
           <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="0" page="16"/>
          </pdf2:Link>
          <bfo:content mcid="28" page="16">.</bfo:content>
         </ns3:text>
        </ns3:text-unit>
       </pdf2:LBody>
      </pdf2:LI>
     </ns3:enumerate>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01211">
     <ns3:subsubsection id="ID.01212">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01213">
       <bfo:content mcid="29" page="16">4.2.1 </bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <bfo:content mcid="30" page="16">Generic mode versus lua mode in the mc-task</bfo:content>
     </ns3:subsubsection>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01214">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01215">
       <bfo:content mcid="31" page="16">While in generic mode the commands insert the literals directly and so have all the problems described above the lua mode works quite differently: The tagging commands donâ€™t insert literals but set some </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Em id="ID.01216">
        <bfo:content mcid="32" page="16">attributes</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Em>
       <bfo:content mcid="33" page="16"> which are attached to all the following nodes. When the page is shipped out some lua code is called which wanders through the shipout box and injects the literals at the places where the attributes changes.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01217">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01218">
       <bfo:content mcid="34" page="16">This means that quite a number of problems mentioned above are not relevant for the lua mode:</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01219">
      <ns3:enumerate class="enumerate" id="ID.01220">
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01221">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01222">
         <bfo:content mcid="0" page="17">1.</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01223">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01224">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01225">
           <bfo:content mcid="1" page="17">Pagebreaks between start and end of the marker are </bfo:content>
           <pdf2:Em id="ID.01226">
            <bfo:content mcid="2" page="17">not</bfo:content>
           </pdf2:Em>
           <bfo:content mcid="3" page="17"> a problem. So you can mark a complete paragraph. If a pagebreak occur directly after an start marker or before an end marker this can lead to empty chunks in the PDF and so bloat up PDF a bit, but this is imho not really a problem (compared to the size increase by the rest of the tagging).</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01227">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01228">
         <bfo:content mcid="4" page="17">2.</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01229">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01230">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01231">
           <bfo:content mcid="5" page="17">The commands donâ€™t insert literals directly and so affect line and page breaking much less.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01232">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01233">
         <bfo:content mcid="6" page="17">3.</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01234">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01235">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01236">
           <bfo:content mcid="7" page="17">The numbering of the MCID are done at shipout, so no label/ref system is needed.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01237">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01238">
         <bfo:content mcid="8" page="17">4.</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01239">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01240">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01241">
           <bfo:content mcid="9" page="17">The code can do some marking automatically. Currently everything that has not been marked up by the document is marked as artifact.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
      </ns3:enumerate>
     </ns3:text-unit>
    </pdf2:Sect>
    <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01242">
     <ns3:subsubsection id="ID.01243">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01244">
       <bfo:content mcid="10" page="17">4.2.2 </bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <bfo:content mcid="11" page="17">Commands to mark content and chunks</bfo:content>
     </ns3:subsubsection>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01245">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01246">
       <bfo:content mcid="12" page="17">In generic mode</bfo:content>
       <bfo:content mcid="13" page="17"> is vital that the end command is executed on the same page as the begin command. So think carefully how to place them. For strategies how to handle paragraphs that split over pages see subsection </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Link id="ID.01247">
        <bfo:content mcid="14" page="17">4.2.9</bfo:content>
        <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="0" page="17"/>
       </pdf2:Link>
       <bfo:content mcid="15" page="17">.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <Code id="ID.01248">
      <bfo:content mcid="16" page="17"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="17" page="17">\tagmcbegin{âŸ¨key-val-listâŸ©}</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="18" page="17"/>
     </Code>
     <Code id="ID.01249">
      <bfo:content mcid="19" page="17"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="20" page="17">\tag_mc_begin:n{âŸ¨key-val-listâŸ©}</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="21" page="17"/>
     </Code>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01250">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01251">
       <bfo:content mcid="22" page="17">These commands insert the begin of the marked content code in the PDF. They donâ€™t start a paragraph. </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Em id="ID.01252">
        <bfo:content mcid="23" page="17">They donâ€™t start a group</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Em>
       <bfo:content mcid="24" page="17">. Such markers should not be nested. The command will warn you if this happens.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01253">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01254">
       <bfo:content mcid="25" page="17">The key-val list understands the following keys:</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01255">
      <ns3:description class="description" id="ID.01256">
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01257">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01258">
         <bfo:content mcid="26" page="17">tag</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01259">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01260">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01261">
           <bfo:content mcid="27" page="17">This key is optional. By default the tag name of the surrounding structure is used, which normally should be fine. But if needed the name can be set explicitly with this key. The value of the key is typically one of the standard type listed in section </bfo:content>
           <pdf2:Link id="ID.01262">
            <bfo:content mcid="28" page="17">6</bfo:content>
            <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="1" page="17"/>
           </pdf2:Link>
           <bfo:content mcid="29" page="17"> (without a slash at the begin, this is added by the code). It is possible to setup new tags, see the same section. The value of the key is expanded, so it can be a command. The expansion is passed unchanged to the PDF, so it should with a starting slash give a valid PDF name (some ascii with numbers like H4 is fine).</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01263">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01264">
         <bfo:content mcid="30" page="17">artifact</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01265">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01266">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01267">
           <bfo:content mcid="31" page="17">This will setup the marked content as an artifact. The key should be used for content that should be ignored. The key can take one of the values pagination, pagination/header,pagination/footer, layout, page, background and notype (this is the default). Text in the header and footer should normally be marked with artifact=pagination or pagination/header, pagi-nation/footer but simply artifact (as it is now done automatically) should be ok too.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01268">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01269">
           <bfo:content mcid="32" page="17">It is not quite clear if rules and other decorative graphical objects needs to be marked up as artifacts. Acrobat seems not to mind if not, but PAC 3 complained.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01270">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01271">
           <bfo:content mcid="33" page="17">The validators complain if some text is not marked up, but it is not quite clear if this is a serious problem.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01272">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01273">
           <bfo:content mcid="34" page="17">The</bfo:content>
           <bfo:content mcid="35" page="17"> lua mode will mark up everything unmarked as artifact=notype. You can suppress this behaviour by setting the tagpdfsetup key tagunmarked to false. See section </bfo:content>
           <pdf2:Link id="ID.01274">
            <bfo:content mcid="36" page="17">3.2</bfo:content>
            <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="2" page="17"/>
           </pdf2:Link>
           <bfo:content mcid="37" page="17">.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01275">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01276">
         <bfo:content mcid="38" page="17">stash</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01277">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01278">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01279">
           <bfo:content mcid="39" page="17">Normally marked content will be stored in the â€œcurrentâ€ structure. This may not be what you want. As an example you may perhaps want to put a marginnote behind or before the paragraph it is in the tex-code. With this boolean key the content is marked but not stored in the kid-key of the current structure.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01280">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01281">
         <bfo:content mcid="0" page="18">label</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01282">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01283">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01284">
           <bfo:content mcid="1" page="18">This key sets a label by which you can call the marked content later in another structure (if it has been stashed with the previous key). Internally the label name will start withtagpdf-.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01285">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01286">
         <bfo:content mcid="2" page="18">alt</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01287">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01288">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01289">
           <bfo:content mcid="3" page="18">This key inserts an /Alt value in the property dictionary of the BDC operator. See section </bfo:content>
           <pdf2:Link id="ID.01290">
            <bfo:content mcid="4" page="18">5</bfo:content>
            <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="0" page="18"/>
           </pdf2:Link>
           <bfo:content mcid="5" page="18">. The value is handled as verbatim string, commands are not expanded but the value will be expanded first once (so works like the key alttext-o in previous versions which has been removed). If the value is empty, nothing will happen.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01291">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01292">
           <bfo:content mcid="6" page="18">That means that you can do something like in the following listing and it will insert \frac{a}{b} (hex encoded) in the PDF.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01293">
          <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01294">
           <ns6:codeline id="ID.01295">
            <Code class="justify" id="ID.01296">
             <bfo:content mcid="7" page="18">  \newcommand\myalttext{\frac{a}{b}}</bfo:content>
            </Code>
           </ns6:codeline>
           <ns6:codeline id="ID.01297">
            <Code class="justify" id="ID.01298">
             <bfo:content mcid="8" page="18">  \tagmcbegin{tag=P,alt=\myalttext}</bfo:content>
            </Code>
           </ns6:codeline>
           <ns6:codeline id="ID.01299">
            <Code class="justify" id="ID.01300">
             <bfo:content mcid="9" page="18">  </bfo:content>
            </Code>
           </ns6:codeline>
          </ns6:verbatim>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01301">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01302">
         <bfo:content mcid="10" page="18">actualtext</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01303">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01304">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01305">
           <bfo:content mcid="11" page="18">This key inserts an /ActualText value in the property dictionary of the BDC operator. See section </bfo:content>
           <pdf2:Link id="ID.01306">
            <bfo:content mcid="12" page="18">5</bfo:content>
            <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="1" page="18"/>
           </pdf2:Link>
           <bfo:content mcid="13" page="18">. The value is handled as verbatim string, commands are not expanded but the value will be expanded first once (so works like the key actualtext-o in previous versions which has been removed). If the value is empty, nothing will happen.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01307">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01308">
           <bfo:content mcid="14" page="18">That means that you can do something like in the following listing and and it will insert X (hex encoded) in the PDF.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01309">
          <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01310">
           <ns6:codeline id="ID.01311">
            <Code class="justify" id="ID.01312">
             <bfo:content mcid="15" page="18">   \newcommand\myactualtext{X}</bfo:content>
            </Code>
           </ns6:codeline>
           <ns6:codeline id="ID.01313">
            <Code class="justify" id="ID.01314">
             <bfo:content mcid="16" page="18">   \tagmcbegin{tag=Span,actualtext=\myactualtext}</bfo:content>
            </Code>
           </ns6:codeline>
           <ns6:codeline id="ID.01315">
            <Code class="justify" id="ID.01316">
             <bfo:content mcid="17" page="18">  </bfo:content>
            </Code>
           </ns6:codeline>
          </ns6:verbatim>
         </ns3:text-unit>
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01317">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01318">
           <bfo:content mcid="18" page="18">According to the PDF reference, /ActualText should only be used on marked content sequence of type Span. This is not enforced by the code currently. There is also some discussion going on, if /ActualText can actually be used in a MC dictionary or if it should be in a separate BDC-operator.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01319">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01320">
         <bfo:content mcid="19" page="18">raw</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01321">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01322">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01323">
           <bfo:content mcid="20" page="18">This key allows you to add more entries to the properties dictionary. The value must be correct, low-level PDF. E.g. raw=/Alt (Hello) will insert an alternative Text.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
      </ns3:description>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <Code id="ID.01324">
      <bfo:content mcid="21" page="18"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="22" page="18">\tagmcend</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="23" page="18"/>
     </Code>
     <Code id="ID.01325">
      <bfo:content mcid="24" page="18"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="25" page="18">\tag_mc:end</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="26" page="18"/>
     </Code>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01326">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01327">
       <bfo:content mcid="27" page="18">These commands insert the end code of the marked content. They donâ€™t end a group and it doesnâ€™t matter if they are in another group as the starting commands. In generic mode both commands check if there has been a begin marker and issue a warning if not. In luamode it is often possible to omit the command, as the effect of the begin command ends with a new \tagmcbegin anyway.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <Code id="ID.01328">
      <bfo:content mcid="28" page="18"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="29" page="18">\tagmcuse</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="30" page="18"/>
     </Code>
     <Code id="ID.01329">
      <bfo:content mcid="31" page="18"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="32" page="18">\tag_mc_use:n</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="33" page="18"/>
     </Code>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01330">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01331">
       <bfo:content mcid="34" page="18">These commands allow you to record a marked content that you stashed away into the current structure. Be aware that a marked content can be used only once â€“ the command will warn you if you try to use it a second time.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <Code id="ID.01332">
      <bfo:content mcid="0" page="19"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="1" page="19">\tag_mc_end_push:</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="2" page="19"/>
     </Code>
     <Code id="ID.01333">
      <bfo:content mcid="3" page="19"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="4" page="19">\tag_mc_begin_pop:n{âŸ¨key-val-listâŸ©}</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="5" page="19"/>
     </Code>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01334">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01335">
       <bfo:content mcid="6" page="19">If there is an open mc chunk, the first command ends it and pushes its tag on a stack. If there is no open chunk, it puts âˆ’1 on the stack (for debugging). The second command removes a value from the stack. If it is different from âˆ’1 it opens a tag with it. The command is mainly meant to be used inside hooks and command definitions so there is only an expl3 version. Perhaps other content of the mc-dictionary (for example the Lang) needs to be saved on the stacked too.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <Code id="ID.01336">
      <bfo:content mcid="7" page="19"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="8" page="19">\tagmcifinTF{âŸ¨true codeâŸ©}{âŸ¨false codeâŸ©}</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="9" page="19"/>
     </Code>
     <Code id="ID.01337">
      <bfo:content mcid="10" page="19"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="11" page="19">\tag_mc_if_in:TF{âŸ¨true codeâŸ©}{âŸ¨false codeâŸ©}</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="12" page="19"/>
     </Code>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01338">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01339">
       <bfo:content mcid="13" page="19">These commands check if a marked content is currently open and allows you to e.g. add the end marker if yes.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01340">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01341">
       <bfo:content mcid="14" page="19">In </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Em id="ID.01342">
        <bfo:content mcid="15" page="19">generic mode</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Em>
       <bfo:content mcid="16" page="19">, where marked content command shouldnâ€™t be nested, it works with a global boolean.</bfo:content>

      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01344">

       </pdf2:Em>
       <bfo:content mcid="19" page="19"> it tests if the mc-attribute is currently unset. You canâ€™t test the nesting level with it!</bfo:content>

    <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01346">
     <ns3:subsubsection id="ID.01347">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01348">
       <bfo:content mcid="20" page="19">4.2.3 </bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <bfo:content mcid="21" page="19">Retrieving data</bfo:content>
     </ns3:subsubsection>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01349">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01350">
       <bfo:content mcid="22" page="19">With more elaborate tagging the need arise to retrieve and store current data.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <Code id="ID.01351">
      <bfo:content mcid="23" page="19"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="24" page="19">\tag_get:n{âŸ¨key wordâŸ©}</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="25" page="19"/>
     </Code>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01352">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01353">
       <bfo:content mcid="26" page="19">This (expandable) command give back some variables. Currently the working key words are mc_tag, struct_tag, struct_id and struct_num. The ID is a string and returned including parentheses. struct_num returns a number and works also if only tagpdf-base has been loaded, but then doesnâ€™t give the same output: if tagpdf is loaded and tagging is active, struct_num gives the number of currently active structure, so it reverts to the parent number if a structure is closed. If only tagpdf-base is loaded nesting of structure is not tracked and so the command gives back the number of the last structure that has been created.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
    </pdf2:Sect>
    <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01354">
     <ns3:subsubsection id="ID.01355">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01356">
       <bfo:content mcid="27" page="19">4.2.4 </bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <bfo:content mcid="28" page="19">Luamode: global or not global â€“ that is the question</bfo:content>
     </ns3:subsubsection>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01357">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01358">
       <bfo:content mcid="29" page="19">In</bfo:content>
       <bfo:content mcid="30" page="19"> luamode the mc-commands set and unset an attribute to mark the nodes. One can view such an attribute like a font change or a color: they affect all following chars and glue nodes until stopped.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01359">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01360">
       <bfo:content mcid="31" page="19">From version 0.6 to 0.82 the attributes were set locally. This had the advantage that the attributes didnâ€™t spill over in area where they are not wanted like the header and footer or the background pictures. But it had the disadvantage that it was difficult for an inner structure to correctly interrupt the outer mc-chunk if it canâ€™t control the group level. For example this didnâ€™t work due to the grouping inserted by the user:</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01361">
      <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01362">
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01363">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01364">

        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01365">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01366">

       </ns6:codeline>

       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01369">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01370">

        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01371">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01372">
         <bfo:content mcid="36" page="19">   \tag_mc_end_push:</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01373">

       </ns6:codeline>

       </ns6:codeline>

       </ns6:codeline>

        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01386">
         <bfo:content mcid="6" page="20">  }% user grouping</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01387">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01388">
         <bfo:content mcid="7" page="20"> Continuation of paragraph</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01389">

      </ns6:verbatim>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01393">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01394">
       <bfo:content mcid="10" page="20">The reading order was then wrong, and the </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Em id="ID.01395">
        <bfo:content mcid="11" page="20">emphasized text</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Em>
       <bfo:content mcid="12" page="20"> moved in the structure at the end.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01396">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01397">
       <bfo:content mcid="13" page="20">So starting with version 0.9 this has been reverted. The attribute is now global again. This solves the â€œ interruptionâ€ problem, but has its price: Material inserted by the output routine must be properly guarded. For example</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>

     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01428">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01429">
       <bfo:content mcid="28" page="20">Here the header and the background code on the </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Em id="ID.01430">
        <bfo:content mcid="29" page="20">first</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Em>
       <bfo:content mcid="30" page="20"> page will be marked up as paragraph and added as chunk to the document structure. The header and the background code on the </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Em id="ID.01431">
        <bfo:content mcid="31" page="20">second</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Em>
       <bfo:content mcid="32" page="20"> page will be marked as artifact. The following figure shows how the tags looks like.</bfo:content>

      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01433">
       <pdf2:Figure Layout:BBox="[104.2362 223.2727 269.8358 330.0725]" alt="Show tags of examples" id="ID.01434">
