         <bfo:blob BitsPerComponent="8" ColorSpace="DeviceRGB" Height="178" Length="147384" Subtype="Image" Type="XObject" Width="276" content="image"/>
        </bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Figure>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01435">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01436">
       <bfo:content mcid="34" page="20">It is therefore from now on important to correctly markup such code. Header and footer typically should be artifacts. The LaTeX kernel hasnâ€™t yet suitable hooks around header and footer to allow to automate this, but a first draft has been added with pdfmanagement-testphase. Starting with version 0.92 header and footer are marked as (simple) artifacts. If they contain code which needs a different markup it still must be added explicitly. With packages likefancyhdr or scrlayer-scrpage it is quite easy to add the needed code.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
    </pdf2:Sect>
    <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01437">
     <ns3:subsubsection id="ID.01438">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01439">
       <bfo:content mcid="3" page="21">4.2.5 </bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <bfo:content mcid="4" page="21">Tips</bfo:content>
     </ns3:subsubsection>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01440">
      <ns3:itemize class="itemize" id="ID.01441">
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01442">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01443">
         <bfo:content mcid="5" page="21">â€¢</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01444">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01445">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01446">
           <bfo:content mcid="6" page="21">Mark commands inside floats should work fine (but need perhaps some compilation rounds in generic mode).</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01447">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01448">
         <bfo:content mcid="7" page="21">â€¢</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01449">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01450">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01451">
           <bfo:content mcid="8" page="21">In case you want to use it inside a \savebox (or some command that saves the text inter-nally in a box): If the box is used directly, there is probably no problem. If the use is later, stash the marked content and add the needed \tagmcuse directly before oder after the box when you use it.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01452">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01453">
         <bfo:content mcid="9" page="21">â€¢</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01454">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01455">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01456">
           <bfo:content mcid="10" page="21">Donâ€™t use a saved box with markers twice.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01457">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01458">
         <bfo:content mcid="11" page="21">â€¢</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01459">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01460">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01461">
           <bfo:content mcid="12" page="21">If boxes are unboxed you will have to analyze the PDF to check if everything is ok.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01462">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01463">
         <bfo:content mcid="13" page="21">â€¢</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01464">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01465">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01466">
           <bfo:content mcid="14" page="21">If you use complicated structures and commands (breakable boxes like the one from tcolorbox, multicol, many footnotes) you will have to check the PDF.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
      </ns3:itemize>
     </ns3:text-unit>
    </pdf2:Sect>
    <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01471">
     <ns3:subsubsection id="ID.01472">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01473">
       <bfo:content mcid="15" page="21">4.2.6 </bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <bfo:content mcid="16" page="21">Header and Footer</bfo:content>
     </ns3:subsubsection>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01474">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01475">
       <bfo:content mcid="17" page="21">Tagging header and footer is not trivial. At first on the technical side header and footer are typeset and attached to the page during the output routine and the exact timing is not really under control of the user. That means that when adding tagging there one has to be careful not to disturb the tagging of the main textâ€”this is mostly important in luamode where the attributes are global and can easily spill over.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01476">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01477">
       <bfo:content mcid="0" page="22">At second one has to decide about how to tag: in many cases header and footer can simply be ignored, they only contain information which are meant to visually guide the reader and so are not relevant for the structure. This means that normally they should be tagged as artifacts. The PDF reference offers here a rather large number of options here to describe different versions of â€œ ignore thisâ€. Typically the header and footer should get the type Pagination and this types has a number of subtypes like Header, Footer, PageNum. It is not yet known if any technology actually make use of this info.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01478">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01479">
       <bfo:content mcid="1" page="22">But they can also contain meaningful content, for example an address. In such cases the content should be added to the structure (where?) but even if this address is repeated on every page at best only once. All this need some thoughts both from the users and the packages and code providing support for header and footers.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01480">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01481">
       <bfo:content mcid="2" page="22">For now tagpdf added some first support for automatically tagging: Starting with version 0.92 header and footer are by default automatically marked up as (simple) artifacts.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01482">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01483">
       <bfo:content mcid="3" page="22">With the key exclude-header-footer the behaviour can be changed: The value false disables the automatic tagging, the value pagination add additionally an /Artifact structure with the attribute /Pagination.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01484">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01485">
       <bfo:content mcid="4" page="22">If some additional markup (or even a structure) is wanted, something like this should be used (here with the syntax of the fancyhdr package) to close the open mc-chunk and restart if after the content:</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01486">
      <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01487">
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01488">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01489">
         <bfo:content mcid="5" page="22">\ExplSyntaxOn</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01490">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01491">
         <bfo:content mcid="6" page="22">\cfoot{\leavevmode</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01492">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01493">
         <bfo:content mcid="7" page="22">  \tag_mc_end_push:</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01494">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01495">
         <bfo:content mcid="8" page="22">   \tagmcbegin{artifact=pagination/footer}</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01496">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01497">
         <bfo:content mcid="9" page="22">     \thepage</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01498">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01499">
         <bfo:content mcid="10" page="22">   \tagmcend</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01500">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01501">
         <bfo:content mcid="11" page="22">  \tag_mc_begin_pop:n{artifact}}</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01502">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01503">
         <bfo:content mcid="12" page="22">\ExplSyntaxOff</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
      </ns6:verbatim>
     </ns3:text-unit>
    </pdf2:Sect>
    <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01504">
     <ns3:subsubsection id="ID.01505">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01506">
       <bfo:content mcid="13" page="22">4.2.7 </bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <bfo:content mcid="14" page="22">Links and other annotations</bfo:content>
     </ns3:subsubsection>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01507">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01508">
       <bfo:content mcid="15" page="22">Annotations (like links or form field annotations) are objects associated with a geometric region of the page rather than with a particular object in its content stream. Any connection between a link or a form field and the text is based solely on visual appearance (the link text is in the same region, or there is empty space for the form field annotation) rather than on an explicitly specified association.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01509">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01510">
       <bfo:content mcid="16" page="22">To connect such a annotation with the structure and so with surrounding or underlying text a specific structure has to be added, see </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Link id="ID.01511">
        <bfo:content mcid="17" page="22">3</bfo:content>
        <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="0" page="22"/>
       </pdf2:Link>
       <bfo:content mcid="18" page="22">: The annotation is added to a structure element as an object reference. It is not referenced directly but through an intermediate object of type OBJR. To the dictionary of the annotation a /StructParent entry must be added, the value is a number which is then used in the ParentTree to define a relationship between the annotation and the parent structure element.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01512">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01513">
       <bfo:content mcid="19" page="22">To support this, tagpdf offers currently two commands</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <Code id="ID.01514">
      <bfo:content mcid="20" page="22"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="21" page="22">\tag_struct_parent_int:</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="22" page="22"/>
     </Code>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01515">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01516">
       <bfo:content mcid="23" page="22">This insert the current value of a global counter used to track such objects. It can be used to add the /StructParent value to the annotation dictionary.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <Code id="ID.01517">
      <bfo:content mcid="0" page="23"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="1" page="23">\tag_struct_insert_annot:nn{âŸ¨object referenceâŸ©}{âŸ¨struct parent numberâŸ©}</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="2" page="23"/>
     </Code>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01518">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01519">
       <bfo:content mcid="3" page="23">This will insert the annotation described by the object reference into the current structure by creating the OBJR object. It will also add the necessary entry to the parent tree and increase the global counter referred to by \tag_struct_parent_int:. It does nothing if (structure) tagging is not activated.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01520">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01521">
       <bfo:content mcid="4" page="23">Attention! As the second command increases the global counter at the end it changes the value given back by the first. That means that if nesting is involved care must be taken that the correct numbers is used. This should be easy to fulfil for most annotations, as there are boxes. There the second command should at best be used directly behind the annotation and it can make use of \tag_struct_parent_int:. For links nesting is theoretically possible, and it could be that future versions need more sophisticated handling here.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01522">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01523">
       <bfo:content mcid="5" page="23">In environments which process their content twice like tabularx or align it would be the best to exclude the second command from the trial step, but this will need better support from these environments.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01524">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01525">
       <bfo:content mcid="6" page="23">Typically using this commands is not often needed: Since version 0.81 tagpdf already handles (unnested) links, and form fields created with the l3pdffield-testphase package will be handle by this package.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01526">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01527">
       <bfo:content mcid="7" page="23">The following listing shows low-level to create link where the two commands are used:</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01528">
      <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01529">
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01530">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01531">
         <bfo:content mcid="8" page="23">\pdfextension startlink</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01532">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01533">
         <bfo:content mcid="9" page="23">    attr</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01534">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01535">
         <bfo:content mcid="10" page="23">     {</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01536">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01537">
         <bfo:content mcid="11" page="23">     /StructParent \tag_struct_parent_int: %&lt;----</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01538">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01539">
         <bfo:content mcid="12" page="23">     }</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01540">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01541">
         <bfo:content mcid="13" page="23">    user {</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01542">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01543">
         <bfo:content mcid="14" page="23">          /Subtype/Link</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01544">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01545">
         <bfo:content mcid="15" page="23">          /A</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01546">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01547">
         <bfo:content mcid="16" page="23">           &lt;&lt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01548">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01549">
         <bfo:content mcid="17" page="23">            /Type/Action</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01550">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01551">
         <bfo:content mcid="18" page="23">            /S/URI</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01552">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01553">
         <bfo:content mcid="19" page="23">            /URI(http://www.dante.de)</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01554">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01555">
         <bfo:content mcid="20" page="23">           &gt;&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01556">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01557">
         <bfo:content mcid="21" page="23">         }</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01558">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01559">
         <bfo:content mcid="22" page="23">    This is a link.</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01560">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01561">
         <bfo:content mcid="23" page="23">\pdfextension endlink</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01562">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01563">
         <bfo:content mcid="24" page="23">\tag_struct_insert_annot:xx {\pdfannot_link_ref_last:}{\tag_struct_parent_int:}</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
      </ns6:verbatim>
     </ns3:text-unit>
    </pdf2:Sect>
    <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01564">
     <ns3:subsubsection id="ID.01565">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01566">
       <bfo:content mcid="25" page="23">4.2.8 </bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <bfo:content mcid="26" page="23">Math</bfo:content>
     </ns3:subsubsection>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01567">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01568">
       <bfo:content mcid="27" page="23">Math is a problem. I have seen an example where </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Em id="ID.01569">
        <bfo:content mcid="28" page="23">every single symbol</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Em>
       <bfo:content mcid="29" page="23"> has been marked up with tags from MathML along with an /ActualText entry and an entry with alternate text which describes how to read the symbol. The PDF then looked like this</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01570">
      <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01571">
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01572">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01573">
         <bfo:content mcid="30" page="23">/mn &lt;&lt;/MCID 6 /ActualText&lt;FEFF0034&gt;/Alt(  : open bracket: four )&gt;&gt;BDC</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01574">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01575">
         <bfo:content mcid="31" page="23">...</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01576">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01577">
         <bfo:content mcid="32" page="23">/mn &lt;&lt;/MCID 7 /ActualText&lt;FEFF0033&gt;/Alt(  third s  )&gt;&gt;BDC</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01578">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01579">
         <bfo:content mcid="33" page="23">...</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01580">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01581">
         <bfo:content mcid="34" page="23">/mo &lt;&lt;/MCID 8 /ActualText&lt;FEFF2062&gt;/Alt(  times  )&gt;&gt;BDC</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
      </ns6:verbatim>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01582">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01583">
       <bfo:content mcid="0" page="24">If this is really the way to go one would need some script to add the mark-up as doing it manually is too much work and would make the source unreadable â€“ at least with pdflatex and the generic mode. In lua mode is it possible to hook into the mlist_to_hlist callback and add marker automatically. Some first implementation is done by Marcel KrÃ¼ger in the luamml project.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01584">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01585">
       <bfo:content mcid="1" page="24">But Iâ€™m not sure that this is the best way to do math. It looks rather odd that a document should have to tell a screen reader in such detail how to read an equation. It would be much more efficient, sensible and flexible if a complete representation of the equation in mathML could be stored in the PDF and the task how to read this aloud delegated to the screen reader. As PDF 2.0 introduced associated files it is probable that this will be the way to go but more investigations are needed here.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01586">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01587">
       <bfo:content mcid="2" page="24">See also section </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Link id="ID.01588">
        <bfo:content mcid="3" page="24">5</bfo:content>
        <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="0" page="24"/>
       </pdf2:Link>
       <bfo:content mcid="4" page="24"> for some more remarks and tests.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
    </pdf2:Sect>
    <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01589">
     <ns3:subsubsection id="ID.01590">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01591">
       <bfo:content mcid="5" page="24">4.2.9 </bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <bfo:content mcid="6" page="24">Split paragraphs</bfo:content>
     </ns3:subsubsection>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01592">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01593">
       <bfo:content mcid="7" page="24">A</bfo:content>
       <bfo:content mcid="8" page="24"> problem in generic mode are paragraphs with page breaks. As already mentioned the end marker EMC must be added on the same page as the begin marker. But it is in pdflatex </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Em id="ID.01594">
        <bfo:content mcid="9" page="24">very</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Em>
       <bfo:content mcid="10" page="24">difficult to inject something at the page break automatically. One can manipulate the shipout box to some extend in the output routine, but this is not easy and it gets even more difficult if inserts like footnotes and floats are involved: the end of the paragraph is then somewhere in the middle of the box.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01595">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01596">
       <bfo:content mcid="11" page="24">So with pdflatex in generic mode one until now had to do the splitting manually.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01597">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01598">
       <bfo:content mcid="12" page="24">The example mc-manual-para-split demonstrates how this can be done. The general idea was to use \vadjust in the right place:</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01599">
      <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01600">
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01601">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01602">
         <bfo:content mcid="13" page="24">\tagmcbegin{tag=P}</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01603">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01604">
         <bfo:content mcid="14" page="24">...</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01605">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01606">
         <bfo:content mcid="15" page="24">fringilla, ligula wisi commodo felis, ut adipiscing felis dui in</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01607">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01608">
         <bfo:content mcid="16" page="24">enim. Suspendisse malesuada ultrices ante.% page break</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01609">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01610">
         <bfo:content mcid="17" page="24">\vadjust{\tagmcend\pagebreak\tagmcbegin{tag=P}}</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01611">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01612">
         <bfo:content mcid="18" page="24">Pellentesque scelerisque</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01613">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01614">
         <bfo:content mcid="19" page="24">...</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01615">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01616">
         <bfo:content mcid="20" page="24">sit amet, lacus.\tagmcend</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
      </ns6:verbatim>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01617">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01618">
       <bfo:content mcid="21" page="24">Starting with version 0.92 there is code which tries to resolve this problem. Basically it works like this: every mc-command issues a mark command (actually two slightly different). When the page is built in the output routine this mark commands are inspected and from them </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Span ActualText="LaTeX" id="ID.01619">
        <bfo:content mcid="22" page="24">LATEX</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Span>
       <bfo:content mcid="23" page="24"> can deduce if there is a mc-chunk which must be closed or reopened. The method is described in Frank Mittelbachâ€™s talk at TUG 2021 â€œ Taming the beast â€” Advances in paragraph tagging with pdfTeX and XeTeXâ€ </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Link id="ID.01620">
        <bfo:content mcid="24" page="24">https://youtu.be/SZHIeevyo3U?t=19551</bfo:content>
        <bfo:annotation alt="url" index="1" page="24"/>
       </pdf2:Link>
       <bfo:content mcid="25" page="24">.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01621">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01622">
       <bfo:content mcid="26" page="24">Please note</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01623">
      <ns3:itemize class="itemize" id="ID.01624">
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01625">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01626">
         <bfo:content mcid="27" page="24">â€¢</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01627">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01628">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01629">
           <bfo:content mcid="28" page="24">The code requires a pdfmanagement-testphase version v0.95i or newer.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01630">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01631">
         <bfo:content mcid="29" page="24">â€¢</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01632">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01633">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01634">
           <bfo:content mcid="30" page="24">Typically you will need more compilations than previously, donâ€™t rely on the rerun mes-sages, but if something looks wrong rerun.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01635">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01636">
         <bfo:content mcid="31" page="24">â€¢</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01637">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01638">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01639">
           <bfo:content mcid="32" page="24">The code relies on that related \tagmcbegin and \tagmcend are in the same boxing level. If one is in a box (which hides the marks) and the other in the main galley, things will go wrong.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
      </ns3:itemize>
     </ns3:text-unit>
    </pdf2:Sect>
    <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01640">
     <ns3:subsubsection id="ID.01641">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01642">
       <bfo:content mcid="0" page="25">4.2.10 </bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <bfo:content mcid="1" page="25">Automatic tagging of paragraphs</bfo:content>
     </ns3:subsubsection>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01643">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01644">
       <bfo:content mcid="2" page="25">Another feature that emerged from the </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Span ActualText="LaTeX" id="ID.01645">
        <bfo:content mcid="3" page="25">LATEX</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Span>
       <bfo:content mcid="4" page="25"> tagged PDF project are hooks at the begin and end of paragraphs. tagpdf makes use of these hooks to tag paragraphs. In the first version it added only one structure, but this proved to be not adequate:</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01646">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01647">
       <bfo:content mcid="5" page="25">Paragraphs in </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Span ActualText="LaTeX" id="ID.01648">
        <bfo:content mcid="6" page="25">LATEX</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Span>
       <bfo:content mcid="7" page="25"> can be nested, e.g., you can have a paragraph containing a display quote, which in turn consists of more than one (sub)paragraph, followed by some more text which all belongs to the same outer paragraph.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01649">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01650">
       <bfo:content mcid="8" page="25">In the PDF model and in the HTML model that is not supported: the rules in PDF specifica-tion do not allow P-structures to be nested â€” a limitation that conflicts with real live, given that such constructs are quite normal in spoken and written language.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01651">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01652">
       <bfo:content mcid="9" page="25">The approach we take (starting with march 2023, version 0.98e) to resolve this is to model such â€œ bigâ€ paragraphs with a structure named text-unit and use P (under the name text) only for (portions of) the actual paragraph text in a way that the Ps are not nested. As a result we have for a simple paragraph two structures:</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01653">
      <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01654">
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01655">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01656">
         <bfo:content mcid="10" page="25">&lt;text-unit&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01657">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01658">
         <bfo:content mcid="11" page="25">  &lt;P&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01659">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01660">
         <bfo:content mcid="12" page="25">   The paragraph text ...</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01661">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01662">
         <bfo:content mcid="13" page="25">  &lt;/P&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01663">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01664">
         <bfo:content mcid="14" page="25">&lt;/text-unit</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
      </ns6:verbatim>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01665">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01666">
       <bfo:content mcid="15" page="25">In the case of an element, such as a display quote or a display list inside the paragraph, we then have</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
      <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01667">
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01668">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01669">
         <bfo:content mcid="16" page="25">&lt;text-unit&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01670">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01671">
         <bfo:content mcid="17" page="25">  &lt;text&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01672">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01673">
         <bfo:content mcid="18" page="25">   The paragraph text before the display element ...</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01674">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01675">
         <bfo:content mcid="19" page="25">  &lt;/text&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01676">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01677">
         <bfo:content mcid="20" page="25">   &lt;display element structure&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01678">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01679">
         <bfo:content mcid="21" page="25">    Content of the display structure possibly involving inner &lt;text-unit&gt; tags</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01680">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01681">
         <bfo:content mcid="22" page="25">   &lt;/display element structure&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01682">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01683">
         <bfo:content mcid="23" page="25">  &lt;text&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01684">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01685">
         <bfo:content mcid="24" page="25">   ... continuing the outer paragraph text</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01686">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01687">
         <bfo:content mcid="25" page="25">  &lt;/text&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01688">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01689">
         <bfo:content mcid="26" page="25">&lt;/text-unit&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
      </ns6:verbatim>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01690">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01691">
       <bfo:content mcid="27" page="25">In other words such a display block is always embedded in a &lt;text-unit&gt; structure, possibly preceded by a &lt;text&gt;â€¦&lt;/text&gt; block and possibly followed by one, though both such blocks are optional. More information about this can be found in the documentation of latex-lab-block-tagging.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01692">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01693">
       <bfo:content mcid="28" page="25">As a consequence tagpdf now adds two structures if paratagging is activated. The new code to tag display blocks extends this code to handle the nesting of lists and other display structures.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01694">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01695">
       <bfo:content mcid="29" page="25">The automatic tagging require that for every begin of a paragraph with the begin hook code there a corresponding end with the closing hook code. This can fail, e.g if a vbox doesnâ€™t correctly issue a \par at the end. If this happens the tagging structure can get very confused. At the end of the document tagpdf checks if the number of outer and inner start and end paragraph structures created with the automatic paratagging code are equal and it will error if not.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01696">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01697">
       <bfo:content mcid="0" page="26">The automatic tagging of paragraphs can be deactivated completely or only the outer level with the \tagtool keys para and para-flattened or with the (now deprecated) commands \tagpdfparaOn and \tagpdfparaOff.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01698">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01699">
       <bfo:content mcid="1" page="26">Nesting the activation and deactivation of the tagging of paragraphs can be quite difficult. For example if it is unclear if the inner code issues a \par or not it is not trivial to exclude an end hook for every excluded begin hook. In such cases it can be easier to use the paratag key with the value NonStruct to convert some P-structures into NonStruct-structures without real meaning.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
    </pdf2:Sect>
   </pdf2:Sect>
   <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01700">
    <ns3:subsection id="ID.01701">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01702">
      <bfo:content mcid="2" page="26">4.3 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="3" page="26">Task 2: Marking the structure</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01703">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01704">
      <bfo:content mcid="4" page="26">The structure is represented in the PDF with a number of objects of type StructElem which build a tree: each of this objects points back to its parent and normally has a number of kid elements, which are either again structure elements or â€“ as leafs of the tree â€“ the marked contents chunks marked up with the tagmc-commands. The root of the tree is the StructTreeRoot.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01705">
     <ns3:subsubsection id="ID.01706">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01707">
       <bfo:content mcid="5" page="26">4.3.1 </bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <bfo:content mcid="6" page="26">Structure types</bfo:content>
     </ns3:subsubsection>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01708">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01709">
       <bfo:content mcid="7" page="26">The tree should reflect the </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Em id="ID.01710">
        <bfo:content mcid="8" page="26">semantic</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Em>
       <bfo:content mcid="9" page="26"> meaning of the text. That means that the text should be marked as section, list, table head, table cell and so on. A number of standard structure types is predefined, see section </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Link id="ID.01711">
        <bfo:content mcid="10" page="26">6</bfo:content>
        <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="0" page="26"/>
       </pdf2:Link>
       <bfo:content mcid="11" page="26"> but it is allowed to create more. If you want to use types of your own you must declare them. E.g. this declares two new types TAB and FIG and bases them on P:</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01712">
      <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01713">
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01714">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01715">
         <bfo:content mcid="12" page="26">\tagpdfsetup{</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01716">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01717">
         <bfo:content mcid="13" page="26">  add-new-tag = TAB/P,</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01718">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01719">
         <bfo:content mcid="14" page="26">  add-new-tag = FIG/P,</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01720">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01721">
         <bfo:content mcid="15" page="26">            }</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
      </ns6:verbatim>
     </ns3:text-unit>
    </pdf2:Sect>
    <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01722">
     <ns3:subsubsection id="ID.01723">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01724">
       <bfo:content mcid="16" page="26">4.3.2 </bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <bfo:content mcid="17" page="26">Sectioning</bfo:content>
     </ns3:subsubsection>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01725">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01726">
       <bfo:content mcid="18" page="26">The sectioning units can be structured in two ways: a flat, html-like and a more (in pdf/UA2 basically deprecated) xml-like version. The flat version creates a structure like this:</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01727">
      <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01728">
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01729">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01730">
         <bfo:content mcid="19" page="26">&lt;H1&gt;section header&lt;/H1&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01731">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01732">
         <bfo:content mcid="20" page="26">&lt;P&gt; text&lt;/P&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01733">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01734">
         <bfo:content mcid="21" page="26">&lt;H2&gt;subsection header&lt;/H2&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01735">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01736">
         <bfo:content mcid="22" page="26">...</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
      </ns6:verbatim>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01737">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01738">
       <bfo:content mcid="23" page="26">So here the headings are marked according their level with H1, H2, etc.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01739">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01740">
       <bfo:content mcid="24" page="26">In the xml-like tree the complete text of a sectioning unit is surrounded with the Sect tag, and all headers with the tag H. Here the nesting defines the level of a sectioning heading.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01741">
      <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01742">
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01743">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01744">
         <bfo:content mcid="25" page="26">&lt;Sect&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01745">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01746">
         <bfo:content mcid="26" page="26"> &lt;H&gt;section heading&lt;/H&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01747">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01748">
         <bfo:content mcid="27" page="26"> &lt;P&gt; text&lt;/p&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01749">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01750">
         <bfo:content mcid="28" page="26"> &lt;Sect&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01751">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01752">
         <bfo:content mcid="29" page="26">   &lt;H&gt;subsection heading&lt;/H&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01753">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01754">
         <bfo:content mcid="30" page="26">   ...</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01755">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01756">
         <bfo:content mcid="31" page="26"> &lt;/Sect&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01757">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01758">
         <bfo:content mcid="32" page="26">&lt;/Sect&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
      </ns6:verbatim>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01759">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01760">
       <bfo:content mcid="0" page="27">The flat version is more </bfo:content>
       <pdf2:Span ActualText="LaTeX" id="ID.01761">
        <bfo:content mcid="1" page="27">LATEX</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Span>
       <bfo:content mcid="2" page="27">-like and it is rather straightforward to patch \chapter, \section and so on to insert the appropriates Hâ€¦ start and end markers. The xml-like tree is more difficult to automate. If such a tree is wanted I would recommend to use â€“ like the context format â€“ explicit commands to start and end a sectioning unit.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
    </pdf2:Sect>
    <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01762">
     <ns3:subsubsection id="ID.01763">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01764">
       <bfo:content mcid="3" page="27">4.3.3 </bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <bfo:content mcid="4" page="27">Commands to define the structure</bfo:content>
     </ns3:subsubsection>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01765">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01766">
       <bfo:content mcid="5" page="27">The following commands can be used to define the tree structure:</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <Code id="ID.01767">
      <bfo:content mcid="6" page="27"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="7" page="27">\tagstructbegin{âŸ¨key-val-listâŸ©}</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="8" page="27"/>
     </Code>
     <Code id="ID.01768">
      <bfo:content mcid="9" page="27"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="10" page="27">\tag_struct_begin:n{âŸ¨key-val-listâŸ©}</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="11" page="27"/>
     </Code>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01769">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01770">
       <bfo:content mcid="12" page="27">These commands start a new structure. They donâ€™t start a group. They set all their values globally.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01771">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01772">
       <bfo:content mcid="13" page="27">The key-val list understands the following keys:</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01773">
      <ns3:description class="description" id="ID.01774">
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01775">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01776">
         <bfo:content mcid="14" page="27">tag</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01777">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01778">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01779">
           <bfo:content mcid="15" page="27">This is required. The value of the key is normally one of the standard types listed in section </bfo:content>
           <pdf2:Link id="ID.01780">
            <bfo:content mcid="16" page="27">6</bfo:content>
            <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="0" page="27"/>
           </pdf2:Link>
           <bfo:content mcid="17" page="27">. It is possible to setup new tags/types, see the same section. The value can also be of the form type/NS, where NS is the shorthand of a declared name space. Currently the names spaces pdf, pdf2, mathml and user are defined. This allows to use a different name space than the one connected by default to the tag. But normally this should not be needed.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01781">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01782">
         <bfo:content mcid="18" page="27">stash</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01783">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01784">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01785">
           <bfo:content mcid="19" page="27">Normally a new structure inserts itself as a kid into the currently active structure. This key prohibits this. The structure is nevertheless from now on â€œthe current active structureâ€ and parent for following marked content and structures.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01786">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01787">
         <bfo:content mcid="20" page="27">label</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01788">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01789">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01790">
           <bfo:content mcid="21" page="27">This key sets a label by which one can refer to the structure. It is e.g. used by \tag_struct_use:n(where a real label is actually not needed as you can only use structures already defined), and by the ref key (which can refer to future structures). Internally the label name will start with tagpdfstruct- and it stores the two attributes tagstruct (the structure number) and tagstructobj (the object reference).</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01791">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01792">
         <bfo:content mcid="22" page="27">parent</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01793">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01794">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01795">
           <bfo:content mcid="23" page="27">With the parent key one can choose another parent. The value is a structure number which must refer to an already existing, previously created structure. Such a structure number can have been stored previously with \tag_get:n, but one can also use a label on the parent structure and then use \ref_value:nn{tagpdfstruct-label}{tagstruct} to retrieve it.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01796">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01797">
         <bfo:content mcid="24" page="27">alt</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01798">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01799">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01800">
           <bfo:content mcid="25" page="27">This key inserts an /Alt value in the dictionary of structure object, see section </bfo:content>
           <pdf2:Link id="ID.01801">
            <bfo:content mcid="26" page="27">5</bfo:content>
            <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="1" page="27"/>
           </pdf2:Link>
           <bfo:content mcid="27" page="27">. The value is handled as verbatim string and hex encoded. The value will be expanded first once (so works like the key alttext-o in previous versions which has been removed). If the value is empty, nothing will happen.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01802">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01803">
           <bfo:content mcid="28" page="27">That means that you can do something like this:</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01804">
          <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01805">
           <ns6:codeline id="ID.01806">
            <Code class="justify" id="ID.01807">
             <bfo:content mcid="29" page="27">      \newcommand\myalttext{\frac{a}{b}}</bfo:content>
            </Code>
           </ns6:codeline>
           <ns6:codeline id="ID.01808">
            <Code class="justify" id="ID.01809">
             <bfo:content mcid="30" page="27">      \tagstructbegin{tag=P,alt=\myalttext}</bfo:content>
            </Code>
           </ns6:codeline>
           <ns6:codeline id="ID.01810">
            <Code class="justify" id="ID.01811">
             <bfo:content mcid="31" page="27">      </bfo:content>
            </Code>
           </ns6:codeline>
          </ns6:verbatim>
         </ns3:text-unit>
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01812">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01813">
           <bfo:content mcid="32" page="27">and it will insert \frac{a}{b} (hex encoded) in the PDF. In case that the text begins with a command that should not be expanded protect it e.g. with a \empty.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>
       <pdf2:LI id="ID.01814">
        <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01815">
         <bfo:content mcid="0" page="28">actualtext</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:Lbl>
        <pdf2:LBody id="ID.01816">
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01817">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01818">
           <bfo:content mcid="1" page="28">This key inserts an /ActualText value in the dictionary of structure object, see section </bfo:content>
           <pdf2:Link id="ID.01819">
            <bfo:content mcid="2" page="28">5</bfo:content>
            <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="0" page="28"/>
           </pdf2:Link>
           <bfo:content mcid="3" page="28">. The value is handled as verbatim string. The value will be expanded first once (so works like the key alttext-o in previous versions which has been removed). If the value is empty, nothing will happen.</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01820">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01821">
           <bfo:content mcid="4" page="28">That means that you can do something like this:</bfo:content>

           <ns6:codeline id="ID.01824">

           <ns6:codeline id="ID.01828">
            <Code class="justify" id="ID.01829">
             <bfo:content mcid="7" page="28">      </bfo:content>
            </Code>
           </ns6:codeline>
          </ns6:verbatim>
         </ns3:text-unit>
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01830">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01831">
           <bfo:content mcid="8" page="28">and it will insert X (hex encoded) in the PDF. In case that the text begins with a command that should not be expanded protect it e.g. with a \empty</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>

           <bfo:content mcid="28" page="28">This key allows to reference an associated file in the structure element. The value should be the name of an object pointing to the /Filespec dictionary as expected by \pdf_object_ref:n from a current l3kernel. For example:</bfo:content>

             <bfo:content mcid="31" page="28">   \pdffile_embed_file:nnn{example-input-file.tex}{}{tag/AFtest}</bfo:content>
            </Code>
           </ns6:codeline>
           <ns6:codeline id="ID.01883">

           </ns6:codeline>
           <ns6:codeline id="ID.01887">
            <Code class="justify" id="ID.01888">
             <bfo:content mcid="34" page="28">   </bfo:content>
            </Code>
           </ns6:codeline>
          </ns6:verbatim>
         </ns3:text-unit>
         <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01889">
          <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01890">
           <bfo:content mcid="0" page="29">As shown, the wanted AFRelationship can be set by filling the dictionary with the value. The mime type is here detected automatically, but for unknown types it can be set too. See the l3pdffile documentation for details. Associated files are a concept new in PDF 2.0, but the code currently doesnâ€™t check the pdf version, it is your responsability to set it (this can be done with the pdfversion key in \DeclareDocumentMetadata).</bfo:content>
          </ns3:text>
         </ns3:text-unit>
        </pdf2:LBody>
       </pdf2:LI>

     <Code id="ID.01932">
      <bfo:content mcid="17" page="29"/>

      <bfo:content mcid="19" page="29"/>

     <Code id="ID.01933">
      <bfo:content mcid="20" page="29"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="21" page="29">\tag_struct_end:</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="22" page="29"/>
     </Code>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01934">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01935">
       <bfo:content mcid="23" page="29">These commands end a structure. They donâ€™t end a group and it doesnâ€™t matter if they are in another group as the starting commands.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <Code id="ID.01936">
      <bfo:content mcid="24" page="29"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="25" page="29">\tagstructuse{âŸ¨labelâŸ©}</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="26" page="29"/>
     </Code>
     <Code id="ID.01937">
      <bfo:content mcid="27" page="29"/>
      <bfo:content mcid="28" page="29">\tag_struct_use:n{âŸ¨labelâŸ©}</bfo:content>
      <bfo:content mcid="29" page="29"/>
     </Code>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01938">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01939">
       <bfo:content mcid="30" page="29">These commands insert a structure previously stashed away as kid into the currently active structure. A structure should be used only once, if the structure already has a parent you will get a warning.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
    </pdf2:Sect>
    <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01940">
     <ns3:subsubsection id="ID.01941">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01942">
       <bfo:content mcid="31" page="29">4.3.4 </bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <bfo:content mcid="32" page="29">Root structure</bfo:content>
     </ns3:subsubsection>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01943">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01944">
       <bfo:content mcid="33" page="29">A document should have at least one structure which contains the whole document. A suitable tag is Document. Such a root is now always added automatically. Its type can be changed with the key activate.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
    </pdf2:Sect>
    <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01945">
     <ns3:subsubsection id="ID.01946">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01947">
       <bfo:content mcid="0" page="30">4.3.5 </bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <bfo:content mcid="1" page="30">Attributes and attribute classes</bfo:content>
     </ns3:subsubsection>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01948">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01949">
       <bfo:content mcid="2" page="30">Structure Element can have so-called attributes. A single attribute is a dictionary(or a stream but this is currently not supported by the package as I donâ€™t know an use-case) with at least the required key /O (for â€œOwnerâ€ which describes the scope the attribute applies too. As an example here an attribute that can be attached to tabular header (type TH) and adds the info that the header is a column header:</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01950">
      <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01951">
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01952">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01953">
         <bfo:content mcid="3" page="30">&lt;&lt;/O /Table /Scope /Column&gt;&gt;</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
      </ns6:verbatim>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01954">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01955">
       <bfo:content mcid="4" page="30">One or more such attributes can be attached to a structure element. It is also possible to store such an attribute under a symbolic name in a so-called â€œClassedMapâ€ and then to attach references to such classes to a structure.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01956">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01957">
       <bfo:content mcid="5" page="30">To use such attributes you must at first declare it in \tagpdfsetup with the key newattribute. This key takes two argument, a name and the content of the attribute. The name should be a sensible key name, it is converted to a pdf name with \pdf_name_from_unicode_e:n, so slashes and spaces are allow. The content should be a dictionary without the braket.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01958">
      <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01959">
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01960">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01961">
         <bfo:content mcid="6" page="30">\tagpdfsetup</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01962">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01963">
         <bfo:content mcid="7" page="30"> {</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01964">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01965">
         <bfo:content mcid="8" page="30">  newattribute =</bfo:content>
        </Code>
       </ns6:codeline>
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01966">
        <Code class="justify" id="ID.01967">

       </ns6:codeline>

     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01974">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01975">
       <bfo:content mcid="13" page="30">Attributes are only written to the PDF when used, so it is not a problem to predeclare a number of standard attributes.</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01976">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01977">
       <bfo:content mcid="14" page="30">It is your responsability that the content of the dictionary is valid PDF and that the values are sensible!</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01978">
      <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01979">
       <bfo:content mcid="15" page="30">Attributes can then be used with the key attribute or attribute-class which both take a comma list of attribute names as argument:</bfo:content>
      </ns3:text>
     </ns3:text-unit>
     <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01980">
      <ns6:verbatim id="ID.01981">
       <ns6:codeline id="ID.01982">

    </pdf2:Sect>

   <pdf2:Sect id="ID.01990">
    <ns3:subsection id="ID.01991">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.01992">
      <bfo:content mcid="20" page="30">4.4 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="21" page="30">Task 3: tree Management</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01993">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01994">
      <bfo:content mcid="22" page="30">When all the document content has been correctly marked and the data for the trees has been collected they must be flushed to the PDF. This is done automatically (if the package has been activated) with an internal command in an end document hook.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <Code id="ID.01995">
     <bfo:content mcid="23" page="30"/>
     <bfo:content mcid="24" page="30">\__tag_finish_structure:</bfo:content>
     <bfo:content mcid="25" page="30"/>
    </Code>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.01996">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.01997">
      <bfo:content mcid="26" page="30">This will hopefully write all the needed objects and values to the PDF. (Beside the already mentioned StructTreeRoot and StructElem objects, additionally a so-called ParentTree is needed which records the parents of all the marked contents bits, a Rolemap, perhaps a ClassMapand object for the attributes, and a few more values and dictionaries).</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
   </pdf2:Sect>
