    <ns3:subsection id="ID.02101">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02102">
      <bfo:content mcid="4" page="32">4.6 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="5" page="32">Interrupting the tagging</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02103">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02104">
      <bfo:content mcid="6" page="32">Experience showed that it must be possible to interrupt tagging in some places. For example various packages do trial typesetting to measure text and this shouldnâ€™t create structures. There are therefore a number of commands for various use cases</bfo:content>
      <ns3:footnotemark id="ID.02105" ref="[ID.02107]">
       <pdf2:Link id="ID.02106">
        <bfo:content mcid="7" page="32">5</bfo:content>
        <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="0" page="32"/>
       </pdf2:Link>
      </ns3:footnotemark>
      <ns3:footnote id="ID.02107" ref="[ID.02105]">
       <ns3:footnotelabel id="ID.02108">
        <pdf2:NonStruct id="ID.02111">
         <bfo:content mcid="45" page="32">5</bfo:content>
        </pdf2:NonStruct>
       </ns3:footnotelabel>
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02109">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02110">
         <bfo:content mcid="46" page="32">it is quite possible that some of the commands will disappear again if we realize that they are not fitting!</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </ns3:footnote>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <Code id="ID.02112">
     <bfo:content mcid="8" page="32"/>
     <bfo:content mcid="9" page="32">\tag_stop:</bfo:content>
     <bfo:content mcid="10" page="32"/>
    </Code>
    <Code id="ID.02113">
     <bfo:content mcid="11" page="32"/>
     <bfo:content mcid="12" page="32">\tag_start:</bfo:content>
     <bfo:content mcid="13" page="32"/>
    </Code>
    <Code id="ID.02114">
     <bfo:content mcid="14" page="32"/>
     <bfo:content mcid="15" page="32">\tag_stop_group_begin:</bfo:content>
     <bfo:content mcid="16" page="32"/>
    </Code>
    <Code id="ID.02115">
     <bfo:content mcid="17" page="32"/>
     <bfo:content mcid="18" page="32">\tag_start_group_end:</bfo:content>
     <bfo:content mcid="19" page="32"/>
    </Code>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02116">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02117">
      <bfo:content mcid="20" page="32">This commands stop and start tagging in the current group by switching </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Em id="ID.02118">
       <bfo:content mcid="21" page="32">local</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Em>
      <bfo:content mcid="22" page="32"> booleans. The grouping commands also open and close a group.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <Code id="ID.02119">
     <bfo:content mcid="23" page="32"/>
     <bfo:content mcid="24" page="32">\tag_stop:n{âŸ¨labelâŸ©}</bfo:content>
     <bfo:content mcid="25" page="32"/>
    </Code>
    <Code id="ID.02120">
     <bfo:content mcid="26" page="32"/>
     <bfo:content mcid="27" page="32">\tag_start:n{âŸ¨labelâŸ©}</bfo:content>
     <bfo:content mcid="28" page="32"/>
    </Code>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02121">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02122">
      <bfo:content mcid="29" page="32">This commands stop and start tagging in the current group by switching </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Em id="ID.02123">
       <bfo:content mcid="30" page="32">local</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Em>
      <bfo:content mcid="31" page="32"> booleans, but \tag_start:n only restarts if the corresponding tag_stop:n actually stopped something. This is meant for a situation like the following, where you donâ€™t want that the inner \tag_start:n restarts tagging.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02124">
     <ns6:verbatim id="ID.02125">
      <ns6:codeline id="ID.02126">
       <Code class="justify" id="ID.02127">
        <bfo:content mcid="32" page="32">\tag_stop:n{outer}</bfo:content>
       </Code>
      </ns6:codeline>
      <ns6:codeline id="ID.02128">
       <Code class="justify" id="ID.02129">
        <bfo:content mcid="33" page="32"> ...</bfo:content>
       </Code>
      </ns6:codeline>
      <ns6:codeline id="ID.02130">
       <Code class="justify" id="ID.02131">
        <bfo:content mcid="34" page="32"> \tag_stop:n{inner}</bfo:content>
       </Code>
      </ns6:codeline>
      <ns6:codeline id="ID.02132">
       <Code class="justify" id="ID.02133">
        <bfo:content mcid="35" page="32">  ...</bfo:content>
       </Code>
      </ns6:codeline>
      <ns6:codeline id="ID.02134">
       <Code class="justify" id="ID.02135">
        <bfo:content mcid="36" page="32"> \tag_start:n{inner}</bfo:content>
       </Code>
      </ns6:codeline>
      <ns6:codeline id="ID.02136">
       <Code class="justify" id="ID.02137">
        <bfo:content mcid="37" page="32"> ...</bfo:content>
       </Code>
      </ns6:codeline>
      <ns6:codeline id="ID.02138">
       <Code class="justify" id="ID.02139">
        <bfo:content mcid="38" page="32">\tag_start:n{outer}</bfo:content>
       </Code>
      </ns6:codeline>
     </ns6:verbatim>
    </ns3:text-unit>
   </pdf2:Sect>
   <pdf2:Sect id="ID.02140">
    <ns3:subsection id="ID.02141">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02142">
      <bfo:content mcid="39" page="32">4.7 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="40" page="32">Lazy and automatic tagging</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02143">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02144">
      <bfo:content mcid="41" page="32">A number of features of PDF readers need a fully tagged PDF. As an example screen readers tend to ignore alternative text (see section </bfo:content>
      <pdf2:Link id="ID.02145">
       <bfo:content mcid="42" page="32">5</bfo:content>
       <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="1" page="32"/>
      </pdf2:Link>
      <bfo:content mcid="43" page="32">) if the PDF is not fully tagged. Also reflowing a PDF only works for me (even if real space chars are in the PDF) if the PDF is fully tagged (recent versions of the adobe reader manage to reflow also not tagged PDF but it is very slow).</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02146">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02147">
      <bfo:content mcid="44" page="32">This means that even if you donâ€™t care about a proper structure you should try to add at least some minimal tagging. With the now available automatic tagging of paragraphs all that is needed, is to use testphase=phase-II in \DocumentMetadata. With lualatex this can work quite OK if you donâ€™t have unbalanced paragraphs in your document (pdflatex is more fragile).</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
   </pdf2:Sect>
   <pdf2:Sect id="ID.02148">
    <ns3:subsection id="ID.02149">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02150">
      <bfo:content mcid="0" page="33">4.8 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="1" page="33">Adding tagging to commands</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02151">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02152">
      <bfo:content mcid="2" page="33">As mentioned above the mc-markers should not be nested. Basically you write:</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02153">
     <ns6:verbatim id="ID.02154">
      <ns6:codeline id="ID.02155">
       <Code class="justify" id="ID.02156">
        <bfo:content mcid="3" page="33">\tagmcbegin{..}some text ...\tagmcend</bfo:content>
       </Code>
      </ns6:codeline>
      <ns6:codeline id="ID.02157">
       <Code class="justify" id="ID.02158">
        <bfo:content mcid="4" page="33">&lt;optional structure commands&gt;</bfo:content>
       </Code>
      </ns6:codeline>
      <ns6:codeline id="ID.02159">
       <Code class="justify" id="ID.02160">
        <bfo:content mcid="5" page="33">\tagmcbegin{..}some other text\tagmcend</bfo:content>
       </Code>
      </ns6:codeline>
     </ns6:verbatim>
    </ns3:text-unit>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02161">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02162">
      <bfo:content mcid="6" page="33">This is quite workable as long as you mark everything manually. But when defining com-mands you have to ensure that they correctly push and pop the mc-chunks where needed.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
   </pdf2:Sect>
  </pdf2:Sect>
  <pdf2:Sect id="ID.02163">
   <ns3:section id="ID.02164">
    <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02165">
     <bfo:content mcid="7" page="33">5 </bfo:content>
    </pdf2:Lbl>
    <bfo:content mcid="8" page="33">Alternative text, ActualText and text-to-speech software</bfo:content>
   </ns3:section>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02166">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02167">
     <bfo:content mcid="9" page="33">The PDF format allows to add alternative text through the /Alt and the /ActualText key. Both can be added either to the marked content in the page stream or to the object describing the structure.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02168">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02169">
     <bfo:content mcid="10" page="33">The value of /ActualText (inserted by tagpdf with actualtext) is meant to replace single characters or rather small pieces of text. It can be used also without any tagging (e.g. with the package accsupp). If the PDF reader support this (adobe reader does, sumatra not) one can change with it how a piece of text is copied and pasted e.g. to split up a ligature.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02170">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02171">
     <bfo:content mcid="11" page="33">/Alt (inserted by tagpdf with alt) is a key to improve accessibility: with it one can add to a picture or something else an alternative text.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02172">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02173">
     <bfo:content mcid="12" page="33">The file ex-alt-actualtext.tex shows some experiments I made with with both keys and text-to-speech software (the in-built of adobe and nvda). To sum them up:</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02174">
    <ns3:itemize class="itemize" id="ID.02175">
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02176">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02177">
       <bfo:content mcid="13" page="33">â€¢</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02178">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02179">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02180">
         <bfo:content mcid="14" page="33">The keys have an impact on text-to-speech software only if the document is fully tagged.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02181">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02182">
       <bfo:content mcid="15" page="33">â€¢</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02183">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02184">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02185">
         <bfo:content mcid="16" page="33">/ActualText should be at best used around short pieces of marked content.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02186">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02187">
       <bfo:content mcid="17" page="33">â€¢</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02188">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02189">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02190">
         <bfo:content mcid="18" page="33">/Alt is used at best with a structure â€“ this avoids problems with luatex where marked contents blocks can be split over pages.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02191">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02192">
       <bfo:content mcid="19" page="33">â€¢</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02193">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02194">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02195">
         <bfo:content mcid="20" page="33">To some extend one can get a not so bad reading of math with the alternative text.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
    </ns3:itemize>
   </ns3:text-unit>
  </pdf2:Sect>
  <pdf2:Sect id="ID.02196">
   <ns3:section id="ID.02197">
    <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02198">
     <bfo:content mcid="21" page="33">6 </bfo:content>
    </pdf2:Lbl>
    <bfo:content mcid="22" page="33">Standard types and new tags</bfo:content>
   </ns3:section>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02199">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02200">
     <bfo:content mcid="23" page="33">The tags used to describe the type of a structure element can be rather freely chosen. PDF 1.7 and earlier only requires that in a tagged PDF all types should be either from a known set of standard types or are â€œrole mappedâ€ to such a standard type. Such a role mapping is a simple key-value in the RoleMap dictionary.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02201">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02202">
     <bfo:content mcid="24" page="33">So instead of H1 the type section could be used. The role mapping can then be declared with the add-new-tag key:</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02203">
    <ns6:verbatim id="ID.02204">
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.02205">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.02206">
       <bfo:content mcid="25" page="33"> \tagpdfsetup{add-new-tag = section/H1}</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
    </ns6:verbatim>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02207">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02208">
     <bfo:content mcid="26" page="33">In PDF 2.0 the situation is a bit more complicated. At first PDF 2.0 introduced </bfo:content>
     <pdf2:Em id="ID.02209">
      <bfo:content mcid="27" page="33">name spaces</bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Em>
     <bfo:content mcid="28" page="33">. That means that a type can have more than one â€œmeaningâ€ depending on the name space it belongs to. section (name space A) and section (name space B) are two different types.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02210">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02211">
     <bfo:content mcid="29" page="33">At second PDF 2.0 still requires that a tagged PDF maps all types to a standard type, but now there are three sets of standard types (The meanings of the PDF types can be looked up in the PDF-references [1, 4]):</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02212">
    <ns3:enumerate class="enumerate" id="ID.02213">
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02214">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02215">
       <bfo:content mcid="0" page="34">1.</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02216">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02217">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02218">
         <bfo:content mcid="1" page="34">The </bfo:content>
         <pdf2:Em id="ID.02219">
          <bfo:content mcid="2" page="34">standard structure namespace for PDF 1.7</bfo:content>
         </pdf2:Em>
         <bfo:content mcid="3" page="34">, also called the </bfo:content>
         <pdf2:Em id="ID.02220">
          <bfo:content mcid="4" page="34">default standard structure namespace</bfo:content>
         </pdf2:Em>
         <bfo:content mcid="5" page="34">. The public name of the namespace is tag/NS/pdf. This can be used to reference the namespace e.g. in attributes. These are the structure names from PDF 1.7: StructTreeRoot, Document, Part, Sect, Div, Caption, NonStruct, H, H1, H2, H3, H4, H5, H6, P, L, LI, Lbl, LBody, Table, TR, TH, TD, THead, TBody, TFoot, Span, Link, Annot, Figure, Formula, Form, Ruby, RB, RT, Warichu, WT, WP, Artifact, Art, BlockQuote, TOC, TOCI, Index, Private, Quote, Note, Reference, BibEntry, Code, DocumentFragment, Aside, H7, H8, H9, H10, Title, FENote, Sub, Em, Strong</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02221">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02222">
       <bfo:content mcid="6" page="34">2.</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02223">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02224">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02225">
         <bfo:content mcid="7" page="34">The </bfo:content>
         <pdf2:Em id="ID.02226">
          <bfo:content mcid="8" page="34">standard structure namespace for PDF 2.0</bfo:content>
         </pdf2:Em>
         <bfo:content mcid="9" page="34">. The public name of the namespace is tag/NS/pdf2. This can be used to reference the namespace e.g. in attributes. These are more or less same types as in PDF. The following types have been removed from this set:StructTreeRoot, Art, BlockQuote, TOC, TOCI, Index, Private, Quote, Note, Reference, BibEntry, Codeand the following are new:</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02227">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02228">
       <bfo:content mcid="10" page="34">3.</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02229">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02230">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02231">
         <bfo:content mcid="11" page="34">MathML 3.0 as an </bfo:content>
         <pdf2:Em id="ID.02232">
          <bfo:content mcid="12" page="34">other namespaces</bfo:content>
         </pdf2:Em>
         <bfo:content mcid="13" page="34">. The public name of the namespace is tag/NS/mathml. This can be used to reference the namespace e.g. in attributes. There are nearly 200 types in this name space, so I refrain from listing them here.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
    </ns3:enumerate>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02233">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02234">
     <bfo:content mcid="14" page="34">To allow to this more complicated setup the syntax of the add-new-tag key has been ex-tended. It now takes as argument a key-value list with the following keys. A normal document shouldnâ€™t need the extended syntax, the simple syntax section/H1 should in most cases do the right thing.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02235">
    <ns3:description class="description" id="ID.02236">
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02237">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02238">
       <bfo:content mcid="15" page="34">tag</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02239">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02240">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02241">
         <bfo:content mcid="16" page="34">This is the name of the new type as it should then be used in \tagstructbegin.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02242">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02243">
       <bfo:content mcid="17" page="34">tag-namespace</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02244">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02245">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02246">
         <bfo:content mcid="18" page="34">This is the namespace of the new type. The value should be a shorthand of a namespace. The allowed values are currently pdf, pdf2, mathml and user. The default value (and recommended value for a new tag) is user. The public name of the user namespace is tag/NS/user. This can be used to reference the namespace e.g. in attributes.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02247">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02248">
       <bfo:content mcid="19" page="34">role</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02249">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02250">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02251">
         <bfo:content mcid="20" page="34">This is the type the tag should be mapped too. In a PDF 1.7 or earlier this is normally a type from the pdf set, in PDF 2.0 from the pdf, pdf2 or mathml set. It can also be a user type, then this user tag must have been declared before. The PDF format allows mapping to be done transitively. But you should be aware that tagpdf canâ€™t (or more precisely wonâ€™t) check if some unusual role mapping makes really sense, this lies in the responsability of the author.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02252">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02253">
       <bfo:content mcid="21" page="34">role-namespace</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02254">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02255">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02256">
         <bfo:content mcid="22" page="34">The default value is the default namespace of the role: pdf2 for all types in this set, pdf for the type which exist only in PDF 1.7, mathml for the MathML types, and for previously defined user types whatever namespace has been set there. With this key the value can be overwritten.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02257">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02258">
       <bfo:content mcid="23" page="34">unknown key</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02259">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02260">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02261">
         <bfo:content mcid="24" page="34">An unknown key is interpreted as a tag/role, this preserves the old syntax. So this two calls are equivalent:</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02262">
        <ns6:verbatim id="ID.02263">
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02264">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02265">
           <bfo:content mcid="25" page="34">    \tagpdfsetup{add-new-tag = section/H1}</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02266">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02267">
           <bfo:content mcid="26" page="34">    \tagpdfsetup{add-new-tag = {tag=section,role=H1}}</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02268">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02269">
           <bfo:content mcid="27" page="34">   </bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
        </ns6:verbatim>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
    </ns3:description>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02270">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02271">
     <bfo:content mcid="0" page="35">The exact effects of the keys depend on the PDF version. With PDF 1.7 or older the names-pace keys are ignored, with PDF 2.0 the namespace keys are use to setup the correct rolemaps. The namespace key is also used to define the default namespace if the type is used as a role or as tag in a structure.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <pdf2:Sect id="ID.02272">
    <ns3:subsection id="ID.02273">
     <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02274">
      <bfo:content mcid="1" page="35">6.1 </bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Lbl>
     <bfo:content mcid="2" page="35">The latex namespace</bfo:content>
    </ns3:subsection>
    <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02275">
     <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02276">
      <bfo:content mcid="3" page="35">Starting with version 0.98 work has started to setup specific latex tags. In PDF 2.0 in form of a special name space, with PDF 1.7 or older the tags are role mapped. This is work in progress and bound to change.</bfo:content>
     </ns3:text>
    </ns3:text-unit>
   </pdf2:Sect>
  </pdf2:Sect>
  <pdf2:Sect id="ID.02277">
   <ns3:section id="ID.02278">
    <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02279">
     <bfo:content mcid="4" page="35">7 </bfo:content>
    </pdf2:Lbl>
    <bfo:content mcid="5" page="35">Checking parent-child rules</bfo:content>
   </ns3:section>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02280">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02281">
     <bfo:content mcid="6" page="35">The PDF references formulate various rules about whether a structure can be a child of another structure, e.g. a Sect can not be a child of P. In the PDF 1.7 reference this rules were rather vage, in the PDF 2.0 reference there is a quite specific matrix, which sadly misses some of the tags from PDF 1.7. The upcoming ISO norm 32005 will address this problem and extend the matrix to cover tags from PDF 1.7 and 2.0 (but it still misses the math tag and mathml tags).</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02282">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02283">
     <bfo:content mcid="7" page="35">The rules in the matrix are not a simple allowed/not allowed. Instead some rules determine that structure elements can appear only once in a parent, or that additional requirements can be found in the descriptions of the standard structure types, e.g. Caption often has to be the first element in the parent structure, and elements like Part and Div inherit restrictions from parent structures. External standards like PDF/UA can add more rules.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02284">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02285">
     <bfo:content mcid="8" page="35">Altogether this doesnâ€™t make it easy to check if a structure tree is conformant or not without slowing down the compilation a lot.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02286">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02287">
     <bfo:content mcid="9" page="35">With version 0.98 some first steps to do checks (and to react to the result of a change) have been implemented. Some checks will led to warning directly, but the majority will only be visible if the log-level is increased.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02288">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02289">
     <bfo:content mcid="10" page="35">Typical messages will look then like this</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02290">
    <ns6:verbatim id="ID.02291">
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.02292">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.02293">
       <bfo:content mcid="11" page="35">Package tagpdf Info: The rule between parent 'Sect (from Sect/pdf2)'</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>

      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.02296">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.02297">
       <bfo:content mcid="13" page="35"/>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>

      <Code class="justify" id="ID.02299">

     </ns6:codeline>
     <ns6:codeline id="ID.02300">
      <Code class="justify" id="ID.02301">
       <bfo:content mcid="15" page="35">(tagpdf)             and child 'H1 (from section/latex)' is '-1 (âˆ…)'</bfo:content>
      </Code>
     </ns6:codeline>
    </ns6:verbatim>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02302">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02303">
     <bfo:content mcid="16" page="35">The descriptions of the parent and childs are rather verbose as the checks have to take role mapping and name spaces into account. The result of a check is a numberâ€”negative if the relation is not allowed, positive if allowed. The text in the parentheses show the symbols used in the PDF-matrix.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02304">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02305">
     <bfo:content mcid="17" page="35">Be aware</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
    <ns3:itemize class="itemize" id="ID.02306">
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02307">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02308">
       <bfo:content mcid="18" page="35">â€¢</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02309">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02310">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02311">
         <bfo:content mcid="19" page="35">This doesnâ€™t test all rules, it only implements (hopefully correctly) the matrix.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02312">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02313">
       <bfo:content mcid="20" page="35">â€¢</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02314">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02315">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02316">
         <bfo:content mcid="21" page="35">There can be differences between PDF 1.7 and 2.0, e.g. FENote is rolemapped to Note in PDF 1.7 and then has different containment rules.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02317">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02318">
       <bfo:content mcid="22" page="35">â€¢</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02319">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02320">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02321">
         <bfo:content mcid="23" page="35">The special tag MC stands for mc-chunks, so â€œreal contentâ€ (the matrix has containments rules for this too).</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02322">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02323">
       <bfo:content mcid="0" page="36">â€¢</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02324">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02325">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02326">
         <bfo:content mcid="1" page="36">Currently there is as only negative number âˆ’1 but that is bound to change, depending on if (and how) it is possible to â€œrepairâ€ a disallowed parent-child relation.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02327">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02328">
       <bfo:content mcid="2" page="36">â€¢</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02329">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02330">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02331">
         <bfo:content mcid="3" page="36">Warnings can be wrong.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>

    </ns3:itemize>
   </ns3:text-unit>
  </pdf2:Sect>
  <pdf2:Sect id="ID.02332">
   <ns3:section id="ID.02333">
    <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02334">
     <bfo:content mcid="4" page="36">8 </bfo:content>
    </pdf2:Lbl>
    <bfo:content mcid="5" page="36">â€œ Realâ€ space glyphs</bfo:content>
   </ns3:section>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02335">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02336">
     <bfo:content mcid="6" page="36">TeX uses only spaces (horizontal movements) to separate words. That means that a PDF reader has to use some heuristic when copying text or reflowing the text to decide if a space is meant as a word boundary or e.g. as a kerning. Accessible document should use real space glyphs (U+0032) from a font in such places.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02337">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02338">
     <bfo:content mcid="7" page="36">With the key interwordspace you can activate such space glyphs.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02339">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02340">
     <bfo:content mcid="8" page="36">With pdftex this will simply call the primitive \pdfinterwordspaceon. pdftex will then insert at various places a char from a font called dummy-space. Attention! This means that at every space there are additional font switches in the PDF: from the current font to the dummy-space font and back again. This will make the PDF larger. As \pdfinterwordspaceon is a primitive function it canâ€™t be fine tuned or adapted. You can only turn it on and off and insert manually such a space glyph with \pdffakespace.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02341">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02342">
     <bfo:content mcid="9" page="36">With luatex (in luamode) interwordspace is implemented with a lua-function which is inserted in two callbacks and marks up the places where it seems sensible to inter a space glyph. Later in the process the space glyphs are injected â€“ the code will take the glyph from the current font if this has a space glyph or switch to the default latin modern font. The current code works reasonable well in normal text. interwordspace can be used without actually tagging a document.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02343">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02344">
     <bfo:content mcid="10" page="36">The key show-spaces will show lines at the places where in lua mode spaces are inserted and so can help you to find problematic places. For listings â€“ which have a quite specific handling of spaces â€“ you can find a suggestion in the example ex-space-glyph-listings.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02345">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02346">
     <pdf2:Em id="ID.02347">
      <bfo:content mcid="11" page="36">Attention:</bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Em>
     <bfo:content mcid="12" page="36"> Even with real spaces copy&amp; pasting of code doesnâ€™t need to give the correct results: you get spaces but not necessarly the right number of spaces. The PDF viewers I tried all copied four real space glyphs as one space. I only got the four spaces with the export to text or xml in the AdobePro.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <Code id="ID.02348">
    <bfo:content mcid="13" page="36"/>
    <bfo:content mcid="14" page="36">\pdffakespace</bfo:content>
    <bfo:content mcid="15" page="36"/>
   </Code>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02349">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02350">
     <bfo:content mcid="16" page="36">This is in pdftex a primitive. It inserts the dummy space glyph. tagpdf defines this command also for luatex â€“ attention if can perhaps insert break points.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
  </pdf2:Sect>
  <pdf2:Sect id="ID.02351">
   <ns3:section id="ID.02352">
    <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02353">
     <bfo:content mcid="17" page="36">9 </bfo:content>
    </pdf2:Lbl>
    <bfo:content mcid="18" page="36">Structure destinations</bfo:content>
   </ns3:section>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02354">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02355">
     <bfo:content mcid="19" page="36">Standard destinations (anchors for internal links) consist of a reference to a page in the pdf and instructions how to display itâ€”typically they will put a specific coordinate in the left top corner of the viewer and so give the impression that a link jumped to the word in this place. But in reality they are not connected to the content.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02356">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02357">
     <bfo:content mcid="20" page="36">Starting with pdf 2.0 destinations can in a tagged PDF also point to a structure (to a /StructElemobject). GoTo links can then additionally to the /D key which points to a standard page destina-tion also point to such a structure destination with an /SD key. Programs that e.g. convert such a PDF to html can then create better links. (According to the reference, PDF-viewer should prefer the structure destination over the page destination, but as far as it is known this isnâ€™t done yet.)</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02358">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02359">
     <bfo:content mcid="1" page="37">Currently structure destinations (and GoTo links making use of it) could natively only be created with the dvipdfmx backend. With pdftex and lualatex it was only possible to create a restricted type which used only the â€œFitâ€ mode. Starting with </bfo:content>
     <pdf2:Span ActualText="TeX" id="ID.02360">
      <bfo:content mcid="2" page="37">TEX</bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Span>
     <bfo:content mcid="3" page="37">live 2022 (earlier in miktex) both engines will knew new keywords which allow to create structure destination easily.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02361">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02362">
     <bfo:content mcid="4" page="37">Support for this has been already added to the PDF management and tagpdf will make use of it if possible. In most cases it should simply work, but one should be aware that as one now has a destination that is actually tied to the content it gets more important to actually consider the context and the place where such destinations are created. It now makes a difference if the destination is created before the structure is opened or after so in some cases code that place destinations should be changed to place them inside the structure they belong too. One also has to consider the pages connected to the destinations: The structure destination is bound to the page where the structure </bfo:content>
     <pdf2:Em id="ID.02363">
      <bfo:content mcid="5" page="37">begins</bfo:content>
     </pdf2:Em>
     <bfo:content mcid="6" page="37">, if this differ from the page of the page destination (e.g. if the destination is created by a \phantomsection in the middle of a longer paragraph) then may be necessary to surround destinations with a dummy structure (a Span or an Artifact) to get the right page number.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
  </pdf2:Sect>
  <pdf2:Sect id="ID.02364">
   <ns3:section id="ID.02365">
    <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02366">
     <bfo:content mcid="7" page="37">10 </bfo:content>
    </pdf2:Lbl>
    <bfo:content mcid="8" page="37">Accessibility is not only tagging</bfo:content>
   </ns3:section>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02367">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02368">
     <bfo:content mcid="9" page="37">A tagged PDF is needed for accessibility but this is not enough. As already mentioned there are more requirements:</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02369">
    <ns3:itemize class="itemize" id="ID.02370">
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02371">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02372">
       <bfo:content mcid="10" page="37">â€¢</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02373">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02374">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02375">
         <bfo:content mcid="11" page="37">The language must be declared by adding a /Lang xx-XX to the PDF catalog or â€“ if the language changes for a part of the text to the structure or the marked content. Setting the document language can be rather easily done with existing packages. With the new PDF re-source management it should be done with \pdfmanagement_add:nnn{Catalog}{Lang}{(en-US)}. For settings in marked content and structure I will have to add keys.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02376">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02377">
       <bfo:content mcid="12" page="37">â€¢</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02378">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02379">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02380">
         <bfo:content mcid="13" page="37">All characters must have an unicode representation or a suitable alternative text. With lualatex and open type (unicode) fonts this is normally not a problem. With pdflatex it could need</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
        <ns6:verbatim id="ID.02381">
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02382">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02383">
           <bfo:content mcid="14" page="37">      \input{glyphtounicode}</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02384">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02385">
           <bfo:content mcid="15" page="37">      \pdfgentounicode=1</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02386">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02387">
           <bfo:content mcid="16" page="37">      </bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
        </ns6:verbatim>
       </ns3:text-unit>
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02388">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02389">
         <bfo:content mcid="17" page="37">and perhaps some\pdfglyphtounicode commands.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02390">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02391">
       <bfo:content mcid="18" page="37">â€¢</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02392">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02393">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02394">
         <bfo:content mcid="19" page="37">Hard and soft hyphen must be distinct.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02395">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02396">
       <bfo:content mcid="20" page="37">â€¢</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02397">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02398">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02399">
         <bfo:content mcid="21" page="37">Spaces between words should be space glyphs and not only a horizontal movement. See section </bfo:content>
         <pdf2:Link id="ID.02400">
          <bfo:content mcid="22" page="37">8</bfo:content>
          <bfo:annotation alt="ref" index="0" page="37"/>
         </pdf2:Link>
         <bfo:content mcid="23" page="37">.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02401">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02402">
       <bfo:content mcid="24" page="37">â€¢</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02403">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02404">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02405">
         <bfo:content mcid="25" page="37">Various small infos must be present in the catalog dictionary, info dictionary and the page dictionaries, e.g. metadata like title.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
    </ns3:itemize>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02406">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02407">
     <bfo:content mcid="26" page="37">If suitable I will add code for this tasks to this packages. But some of them can also be done already with existing packages like hyperref, hyperxmp, pdfx.</bfo:content>

  </pdf2:Sect>

   <ns3:section id="ID.02409">
    <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02410">
     <bfo:content mcid="0" page="38">11 </bfo:content>
    </pdf2:Lbl>
    <bfo:content mcid="1" page="38">Debugging</bfo:content>
   </ns3:section>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02411">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02412">
     <bfo:content mcid="2" page="38">While developing commands and tagging a document, it can be useful to get some info about the current structure. For this a show command is provided</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <Code id="ID.02413">
    <bfo:content mcid="0" page="37"/>
    <bfo:content mcid="27" page="37">38</bfo:content>
    <bfo:content mcid="3" page="38"/>
    <bfo:content mcid="4" page="38">\ShowTagging{âŸ¨key-valâŸ©}</bfo:content>
    <bfo:content mcid="5" page="38"/>
   </Code>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02414">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02415">
     <bfo:content mcid="6" page="38">This command takes as argument a key-val list which implements a number of show options.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02416">
    <ns3:description class="description" id="ID.02417">
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02418">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02419">
       <bfo:content mcid="7" page="38">mc-data</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02420">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02421">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02422">
         <bfo:content mcid="8" page="38">This key is relevant for luamode only. It shows the data of all mc-chunks created so far. It is accurate only after shipout, so typically should be issued after a newpage. The value is a positive integer and sets the first mc-shown. If no value is given, 1 is used and so all mc-chunks created so far are shown.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02423">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02424">
       <bfo:content mcid="9" page="38">mc-current</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02425">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02426">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02427">
         <bfo:content mcid="10" page="38">This key shows the number and the tag of the currently open mc-chunk. If no chunk is open it shows only the state of the absolute counter. It works in all mode, but the output in luamode looks different.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02428">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02429">
       <bfo:content mcid="11" page="38">struct-stack</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02430">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02431">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02432">
         <bfo:content mcid="12" page="38">This key shows the current structure stack. Typically it will contain at least root and Document. With the value log the info is only written to the log-file, show stops the compilation and shows on the terminal. If no value is used, then the default is show.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>

  <pdf2:Sect id="ID.02597">
   <ns3:section id="ID.02598">
    <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02599">
     <bfo:content mcid="57" page="39">A </bfo:content>
    </pdf2:Lbl>
    <bfo:content mcid="58" page="39">Some remarks about the PDF syntax</bfo:content>
   </ns3:section>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02600">
    <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02601">
     <bfo:content mcid="59" page="39">This is not meant as a full reference only as a background to make the examples and remarks easier to understand.</bfo:content>
    </ns3:text>
   </ns3:text-unit>
   <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02602">
    <ns3:description class="description" id="ID.02603">
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02604">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02605">
       <bfo:content mcid="60" page="39">postfix notation</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02606">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02607">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02608">
         <bfo:content mcid="61" page="39">PDF uses in various places postfix notation. This means that the operator is behind its arguments:</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
       <pdf2:Figure Layout:BBox="[0 0 100 100]" alt="Illustration of postfix notation" id="ID.02609">
        <bfo:content mcid="62" page="39">180obj180R (a reference (operator R) to an object1001100.2742Tm/P&lt;&lt;/MCID 0&gt;&gt;BDC</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Figure>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02610">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02611">
       <bfo:content mcid="0" page="40">Names</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02612">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02613">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02614">
         <bfo:content mcid="1" page="40">PDF knows a sort of variable called a â€œnameâ€. Names start with a slash and may include any regular characters, but not delimiter or white-space characters. Uppercase and lowercase letters are considered distinct: /A and /a are different names. /.notdef and /Adobe#20Green are valid names.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02615">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02616">
         <bfo:content mcid="2" page="40">Quite a number of the options of tagpdf actually define such a name which is later added to the PDF. I recommend </bfo:content>
         <pdf2:Em id="ID.02617">
          <bfo:content mcid="3" page="40">strongly</bfo:content>
         </pdf2:Em>
         <bfo:content mcid="4" page="40"> not to use spaces and exotic chars in such names. While it is possible to escape such names it is rather a pain when moving them through the various lists and commands and quite probably I forgot some place where it is needed.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02618">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02619">
       <bfo:content mcid="5" page="40">Strings</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02620">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02621">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02622">
         <bfo:content mcid="6" page="40">There are two types of strings: </bfo:content>
         <pdf2:Em id="ID.02623">
          <bfo:content mcid="7" page="40">Literal strings</bfo:content>
         </pdf2:Em>
         <bfo:content mcid="8" page="40"> are enclosed in round parentheses. They normally contain a mix of ascii chars and octal numbers:</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02624">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02625">
         <bfo:content mcid="9" page="40">(gr\374\377ehello[]\050\051).</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02626">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02627">
         <pdf2:Em id="ID.02628">
          <bfo:content mcid="10" page="40">Hexadezimal strings</bfo:content>
         </pdf2:Em>
         <bfo:content mcid="11" page="40"> are enclosed in angle brackets. They allow for a representation of all characters the whole unicode ranges. This is the default output of lualatex.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02629">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02630">
         <bfo:content mcid="12" page="40">&lt;003B00600243013D0032&gt;.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02631">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02632">
       <bfo:content mcid="13" page="40">Arrays</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02633">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02634">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02635">
         <bfo:content mcid="14" page="40">Arrays are enclosed by square brackets. They can contain all sort of objects including more arrays. As an example here an array which contains five objects: a number, an object reference, a string, a dictionary and another array. Be aware that despite the spaces 15 0 R is </bfo:content>
         <pdf2:Em id="ID.02636">
          <bfo:content mcid="15" page="40">one</bfo:content>
         </pdf2:Em>
         <bfo:content mcid="16" page="40"> element of the array.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02637">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02638">
         <bfo:content mcid="17" page="40">[0 15 0 R (hello) &lt;&lt;/Type /X&gt;&gt; [1 2 3]]</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
       <pdf2:Figure Layout:BBox="[0 0 100 100]" alt="Illustration of array" id="ID.02639">
        <bfo:content mcid="18" page="40">015 0 R(hello)&lt;&lt;/Type /X&gt;&gt;[1 2 3]</bfo:content>
       </pdf2:Figure>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02640">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02641">
       <bfo:content mcid="19" page="40">Dictionaries</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02642">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02643">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02644">
         <bfo:content mcid="20" page="40">Dictionaries are enclosed by double angle brackets. They contain key-value pairs. The key is always a name. The value can be all sort of objects including more dictionaries. It doesnâ€™t matter in which order the keys are given.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02645">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02646">
         <bfo:content mcid="21" page="40">Dictionaries can be written all in one line:&lt;&lt;/Type/Page/Contents 3 0 R/Resources 1 0 R/Parent 5 0 R&gt;&gt;but at least for examples a layout with line breaks and indentation is more readable:</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02647">
        <ns6:verbatim id="ID.02648">
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02649">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02650">
           <bfo:content mcid="22" page="40">    &lt;&lt;</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02651">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02652">
           <bfo:content mcid="23" page="40">      /Type      /Page</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02653">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02654">
           <bfo:content mcid="24" page="40">      /Contents  3 0 R</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02655">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02656">
           <bfo:content mcid="25" page="40">      /Resources 1 0 R</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02657">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02658">
           <bfo:content mcid="26" page="40">      /MediaBox  [0 0 595.276 841.89]</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02659">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02660">
           <bfo:content mcid="27" page="40">      /Parent    5 0 R</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02661">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02662">
           <bfo:content mcid="28" page="40">    &gt;&gt;</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02663">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02664">
           <bfo:content mcid="29" page="40">    </bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
        </ns6:verbatim>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02665">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02666">
       <bfo:content mcid="30" page="40">(indirect) objects</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02667">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02668">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02669">
         <bfo:content mcid="31" page="40">These are enclosed by the keywords obj (which has two numbers as prefix arguments) and endobj. The first argument is the object number, the second a generation number â€“ if a PDF is edited objects with a larger generation number can be added. As with pdflatex/lualatex the PDF is always new we can safely assume that the number is always 0. Objects can be referenced in other places with the R operator. The content of an object can be all sort of things.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02670">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02671">
       <bfo:content mcid="0" page="41">streams</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02672">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02673">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02674">
         <bfo:content mcid="1" page="41">A stream is a sequence of bytes. It can be long and is used for the real content of PDF: text, fonts, content of graphics. A stream starts with a dictionary which at least sets the/Length name to the length of the stream followed by the stream content enclosed by the keywords stream and endstream.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02675">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02676">
         <bfo:content mcid="2" page="41">Here an example of a stream, an object definition and reference. In the object 2 (a page object) the /Contents key references the object 3 and this then contains the text of the page in a stream. Tf, Tm and TJ are (postfix) operators, the first chooses the font with the name /F15 at the size 10.9, the second displaces the reference point on the page and the third inserts the text.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02677">
        <ns6:verbatim id="ID.02678">
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02679">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02680">
           <bfo:content mcid="3" page="41">  % a page object (shortened)</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02681">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02682">
           <bfo:content mcid="4" page="41">  2 0 obj</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02683">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02684">
           <bfo:content mcid="5" page="41">    &lt;&lt;</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02685">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02686">
           <bfo:content mcid="6" page="41">      /Type/Page</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02687">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02688">
           <bfo:content mcid="7" page="41">      /Contents 3 0 R</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02689">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02690">
           <bfo:content mcid="8" page="41">      /Resources 1 0 R</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02691">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02692">
           <bfo:content mcid="9" page="41">      ...</bfo:content>

         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02701">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02702">
           <bfo:content mcid="14" page="41">  3 0 obj</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02703">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02704">
           <bfo:content mcid="15" page="41">   &lt;&lt;/Length 153 &gt;&gt;</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02705">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02706">
           <bfo:content mcid="16" page="41">   stream</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>

          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>

          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
        </ns6:verbatim>
       </ns3:text-unit>
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02719">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02720">
         <bfo:content mcid="23" page="41">In such a stream the BTâ€“ET pair encloses texts while drawing and graphics are outside of such pairs.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
     </pdf2:LI>
     <pdf2:LI id="ID.02721">
      <pdf2:Lbl id="ID.02722">
       <bfo:content mcid="24" page="41">Number tree</bfo:content>
      </pdf2:Lbl>
      <pdf2:LBody id="ID.02723">
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02724">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02725">
         <bfo:content mcid="25" page="41">This is a more complex data structure that is meant to index objects by numbers. In the core is an array with number-value pairs. A simple version of number tree which has the keys 0 and 3 is</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02726">
        <ns6:verbatim id="ID.02727">
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02728">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02729">
           <bfo:content mcid="26" page="41">6 0 obj</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02730">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02731">
           <bfo:content mcid="27" page="41">&lt;&lt;</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02732">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02733">
           <bfo:content mcid="28" page="41">  /Nums [</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02734">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02735">
           <bfo:content mcid="29" page="41">          0 [ 20 0 R 22 0 R]</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02736">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02737">
           <bfo:content mcid="30" page="41">          3   21 0 R</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02738">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02739">
           <bfo:content mcid="31" page="41">        ]</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02740">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02741">
           <bfo:content mcid="32" page="41">&gt;&gt;</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
         <ns6:codeline id="ID.02742">
          <Code class="justify" id="ID.02743">
           <bfo:content mcid="33" page="41">endobj</bfo:content>
          </Code>
         </ns6:codeline>
        </ns6:verbatim>
       </ns3:text-unit>
       <ns3:text-unit id="ID.02744">
        <ns3:text class="justify" id="ID.02745">
         <bfo:content mcid="0" page="42">This maps 0 to an array and 2 to the object reference 21 0 R. Number trees can be split over various nodes â€“ root, intermediate and leaf nodes. We will need such a tree for the </bfo:content>
         <pdf2:Em id="ID.02746">
          <bfo:content mcid="1" page="42">parent tree</bfo:content>
         </pdf2:Em>
         <bfo:content mcid="2" page="42">.</bfo:content>
        </ns3:text>
       </ns3:text-unit>
      </pdf2:LBody>
